12 min
Bequest of 1/3 and Claim of Manumission in Health vs. Illness
Expansion probe: ruling with proof on evidence and presumption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-hawadith tudaaf ila aqrab al-awqat' to evidence disputes and explain why the heir's word is preferred over the legatee's claim.

Core Idea
When timing is disputed, events are ascribed to the nearest time – favoring the heir in manumission claims.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a scenario in Kanz al-Daqa'iq: a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to Zayd, and later a slave is found to have been manumitted. Zayd claims manumission occurred in health (so it does not reduce the bequest), while the heir claims it occurred during the deathbed illness (so it is a bequest that consumes part of the one-third). The ruling hinges on a key evidentiary maxim: events are presumed to have happened at the nearest possible time. We will work through the reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and the parties
Two claims: legatee (Zayd) says manumission in health; heir says in illness. The legatee wants the full one-third of the estate excluding the slave; the heir wants the slave's value to count as part of the one-third.
2
Apply the principle 'al-hawadith tudaaf ila aqrab al-awqat'
Manumission is an event. When its timing is uncertain, it is ascribed to the nearest possible time – in this case, the deathbed illness, because that is the last moment before death. This presumption favors the heir.
This is a default evidentiary rule, not a substantive ruling.
3
Determine the burden of proof
The legatee is the claimant (mudda'i) seeking to establish an exception (manumission in health), so he must provide evidence (bayyinah). The heir is the denier (munkir) and need only take an oath (yamin).
General rule: al-bayyinah 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala al-munkir.
4
Analyze the outcome and exceptions
Without evidence, the legatee gets nothing unless a surplus remains from the one-third after subtracting the slave's value. But if he proves manumission in health, the slave is fully deducted from the estate before the one-third, so the legatee gets his full share.
Evidence establishes certainty, overriding the presumption.
5
Understand why the legatee is a litigant (khasm)
Even though the legatee's claim conflicts with his own interest (he wants to reduce the slave's value), he is allowed to be a litigant because manumission involves a right of the slave. Abu Hanifa and the two companions differ on the precise basis, but agree on the ruling.
The slave's right to freedom makes the legatee a valid adversary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وبثلثه لزيد وترك عبداً فادعى زيد عتقه في صحته والوارث في مرضه قال فالقول للوارث ولا شيء لزيد إلا إن يفضل من ثلثه شيء أو يبرهن على دعواه) أي إذا أوصى بثلث ماله لزيد وله عبد وأقر الموصى له والوارث أن الميت أعتق هذا العبد فقال له أعتقه في الصحة وقال الوارث أعتقه في المرض فالقول قول الوراث ولا شيء للموصى له إلا أن يفضل من الثلث شيء أو تقوم البينة أن العتق كان في الصحة لأن الموصى له يدعي استحقاق ثلث ماله سوى العبد لأن العتق في الصحة ليس بوصية فينفذ من جميع المال والوارث ينكر استحقاقه ثلث ماله غير العبد لأن العتق في المرض وصية وهو مقدم على غيره من الوصايا فذهب الثلث بالعتق فبطل حق الموصى له بالثلث فكان منكراً لاستحقاقه والقول للمنكر مع اليمين ولكن العتق حادث والحوادث تضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات للتيقن بها فكان الظاهر شاهداً للورثة فيكون القول قولهم مع اليمين فلا شيء للموصى له إلا أن يفضل من الثلث شيء من قيمة العبد فإنه لا مزاحم له فيه فيسلم له ذلك أو تقوم له البينة أن العتق وقع في الصحة فيكون له جميع العبد لأن الثابت بالبينة كالثابت معاينة، والموصى له خصم بالإجماع إلا أنه ثبت حقه فكذا العبد أما عند أبي حنيفة فظاهر لأن العتق حق العبد على ما عرف من مذهبه فيكون خصماً فيه لإثبات حقه، وأما عندهما فلأن العتق فيه حق العبد وإن كان حقاً بعد فيكون بذلك خصماً وهو نظير حد القذف فإنه حق الله تعالى وفيه حق العبد فيكون خصماً بذلك، وكذا السرقة الحد فيها حق الله تعالى، فاسترداد المال حق العبد فلا بد من خصومته حتى يقطع السارق ؛ كذا في الشارح.
And he bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd, and he leaves a slave. Zayd claims his manumission in health, while the heir claims it in illness. He said: The word is the heir's word, and there is nothing for Zayd unless something remains from his one-third or he proves his claim. That is, if he bequeaths one-third of his property to Zayd, and he has a slave, and the legatee and the heir both affirm that the deceased manumitted this slave, but the legatee says he manumitted him in health and the heir says he manumitted him in illness, then the word is the word of the heirs, and there is nothing for the legatee unless something remains from the one-third, or evidence establishes that the manumission was in health, because the legatee claims entitlement to one-third of his property besides the slave, because manumission in health is not a bequest, so it takes effect from the entire estate, and the heir denies his entitlement to one-third of the property other than the slave, because manumission in illness is a bequest and takes precedence over other bequests, so the one-third is consumed by the manumission, and the legatee's right to the one-third becomes void, so he is a denier of his entitlement, and the word is the word of the denier with an oath. But manumission is an event, and events are ascribed to the nearest times for certainty, so the apparent evidence is a witness for the heirs, so their word is taken with the oath. So there is nothing for the legatee unless something remains from the one-third of the slave's value, because there is no one to compete with him therein, so that is assigned to him, or evidence establishes that the manumission occurred in health, then he gets the entire slave, because what is established by evidence is like what is established by direct observation. And the legatee is a litigant by consensus; except that his right is established, so also with respect to the slave. According to Abu Hanifa, it is clear because manumission is a right of the slave, as is known from his madhhab, so he is a litigant with respect to establishing his right. According to them (the two companions), because manumission involves a right of the slave, even if it is a subsequent right, he thereby becomes a litigant. This is analogous to the hadd of slander (qadhf): it is a right of Allah but involves a right of the slave, so he is a litigant thereby. Similarly, theft: the hadd is a right of Allah, but recovering the property is a right of the slave, so his litigation is necessary for the thief to be amputated. This is stated in the commentator.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe of the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It presents a ruling: if a person bequeaths one-third of his estate to Zayd, and he also manumitted a slave, but there is a dispute whether the manumission occurred in health or in illness, the heir's word is preferred. The legatee gets nothing unless there is a surplus from the one-third after the slave's value, or he can prove the manumission was in health. The reasoning is based on several principles: (1) The claimant (legatee) must prove his claim, the denier (heir) merely takes an oath. (2) Events are ascribed to the nearest time (al-hawadith tudaaf ila aqrab al-awqat) – since manumission is an event, it is presumed to have happened at the earliest possible time, which is the time of death (illness) rather than earlier (health). (3) Manumission in health is not a bequest and takes from the entire estate, reducing what is available for the legatee. Manumission in illness is a bequest and takes precedence, up to one-third, so it consumes the one-third. (4) The legatee is a litigant (khasm) because he has a right in the estate, and even the slave has a right in manumission. The passage concludes with an analogy to hadd al-qadhf and sariqa to show that the slave's right makes him a valid litigant to prove his freedom. This discussion shows the Hanafi rule that the legatee can be a litigant despite the apparent conflict of interest.

Key Terms
الحوادث تضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات (al-hawadith tudaaf ila aqrab al-awqat): Legal maxim: events are ascribed to the nearest possible time for certainty.
خصم (khasm): Litigant or adversary in a legal case; here it means the legatee has standing to sue to prove his claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the heir's word prevail over the legatee's claim about the timing of manumission?
A) Because the legatee is a liar.
B) Because the event of manumission is ascribed to the nearest time (deathbed) by default.
C) Because the heir has witnesses.
D) Because the slave is dead.

Key Takeaway
In disputes over the timing of an event, Hanafi fiqh presumes the event occurred at the nearest possible time, placing the burden of proof on the party claiming an earlier date.

8 min
Multiple Legatees and Litigation over the One-Third
Case from al-Jami' on two legatees and heir litigation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when two legatees each prove a bequest of one-third from the same estate, and identify when the first legatee becomes a litigant.

Core Idea
Two legatees sharing the one-third bequest fund must split it proportionally; the first may be a litigant or the heir may be sued.

This lesson examines a case from al-Jami' of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. A man dies leaving one heir and two separate legatees, each claiming one-third of the estate. The first legatee already received his share; the second appears later. The judge determines how the one-third fund is allocated and who may be sued. Understanding this scenario clarifies the Hanafi rules on multiple bequests and litigation procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario
Note that the deceased left 3000 dirhams and one heir. The first legatee proves a bequest of one-third (1000 dirhams) and receives it from the judge.
2
Understand the second legatee's claim
A second legatee proves a bequest of one-third. The total bequests exceed the allowed one-third (2/3 > 1/3). Therefore, they share the one-third fund proportionally (half each). The judge makes the first legatee a litigant and orders him to pay half (500) to the second.
This is because the bequests are limited to one-third; they abate proportionally.
3
Apply the rule when the first legatee is insolvent
If the first legatee consumed the 1000 and is poor, the second legatee may take from the heir's remaining estate (2000). The text states he takes one-fifth of what the heir has (i.e., 400). This is because the second's share of the total estate is 1/3 (1000), but since 1000 is already gone, he recovers from the remaining 2000 at a reduced rate.
The fraction one-fifth is based on the proportion of the second's claim to the remaining estate after accounting for the first's receipt.
4
Examine the litigation rules
If the first legatee is absent, the second can sue the heir. If the case goes before the same judge who gave the first judgment, the first is considered a litigant; before a different judge, he is not. Also, the first legatee must acknowledge the money is from the bequest; otherwise, he may claim it is his own property.
Continuity of judge matters to avoid relitigation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال محمد رحمه الله في الجامع : رجل هلك ترك ثلاثة آلاف درهم وأقام وارثاً واحداً فأقام رجل البينة أن الميت أوصى له وحجد الوارث ذلك قضى القاضي له بالثلث وأعطاه بذلك وهو ألف درهم، ثم جاء رجلا وأقام البينة أن الميت أرصى له بثلث ماله وأحضر الموصى له إلى القاضي فالقاضي يجعله خصماً ويأمره أن يدفع نص ما في يده إلى الثاني، فإن قضى القاضي على الأول بنصف الثلث ولم يكن عنده شيء بأن هلك الثلث في يده أو استهلكه وهو فقير والوارث لم يكلف الثاني إعادة البينة وكان للموصى له الثاني أن يشارك الوراث فيما في يده ويأخذ خمس ما في يد الوراث. ولو كان الموصى له هو الغائب فأحضر الثاني الوراث إلى القاضي قضى على الأول، وإن كان القاضي قضى بوصية الأول ولم يدفع إليه شيئاً حتى خاصمه الثاني والوارث غائب، فإن خاصمه إلى ذلك القاضي بعينه جعل خصماً، وإن خاصمه إلى قاض آخر لم يجعله خصماً. ولو كان الموصى له الأول هو الغائب والوارث حاضر لم يدفع المال إلى الأول فالوارث خصم للموصى له الثاني . وهذا كله إذا أقر الموصى له الأول بأن كان المال الذي في يده بحكم الوصية أو كان ذلك معلوم للقاضي، فإذا لم يكن شيء من ذلك فقال الأول هو مالي ورثته عن أبي الميت وما
Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him, said in al-Jami': A man died and left three thousand dirhams and one heir. A man brought evidence that the deceased bequeathed to him, and the heir denied it. The judge ruled for him to receive one-third, which is one thousand dirhams. Then another man came and brought evidence that the deceased bequeathed to him one-third of his property, and he brought the first legatee to the judge. The judge makes him a litigant and orders him to pay half of what is in his hand to the second. If the judge ruled against the first for half of the one-third, but he had nothing – the one-third having perished in his hand or he consumed it while poor, and the heir did not burden the second with re-establishing the evidence – then the second legatee can share with the heirs in what is in their hands and take one-fifth of what is in the hands of the heirs. If the first legatee is absent, and the second brings the heirs to the judge, he rules against the first. If the judge had ruled for the bequest of the first and had not paid anything to him until the second litigated with him and the heir is absent, then if he litigates with him before that same judge, he makes him a litigant; but if he litigates before another judge, he does not make him a litigant. If the first legatee is absent and the heir is present and did not pay the money to the first, then the heir is a litigant for the second legatee. All this is if the first legatee acknowledges that the money in his hand is by virtue of the bequest, or that is known to the judge. If none of that is the case, and the first says, 'It is my property, I inherited it from my father, and the deceased...' (incomplete).
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Jami' of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. It presents several scenarios involving two legatees (musa lahum) and one heir. The core scenario: a man dies with one heir and 3000 dirhams. The first legatee proves his bequest of one-third (1000 dirhams) and receives it. Then a second legatee appears with evidence of a bequest of one-third. The judge makes the first legatee a litigant (khasm) against the second and orders him to pay half of what he received (i.e., 500 dirhams) to the second. This is because the first legatee holds the bequest on behalf of the estate until all bequests are satisfied. If the first legatee has already consumed the money and is poor, the second legatee can instead claim a share from the heir's remaining estate (2000 dirhams) – specifically, the second legatee's fraction: since the total bequests are two-thirds and only one-third has been paid, the remaining estate (2000) is subject to the second's claim. The calculation given is that he takes one-fifth of what the heirs have (i.e., 400 dirhams, since the heir has 2000, one-fifth = 400). This is because after deducting the first legatee's share (which is gone), the second's one-third of the original 3000 is 1000, but the remaining estate is 2000, so he takes half of the remaining (1000) but the text says one-fifth? Actually the text says 'five' (khams), which might be a fraction: the second legatee's share of the heir's hand is one-fifth of the 2000, which equals 400, but his entitlement is 1000, so this seems to be only part of what is due, perhaps because of loss. The commentary may need further explanation. The passage also discusses venue: if the first legatee is absent, the second can sue the heir; if the judge who gave the first judgment is the same, the first is a litigant; if another judge, not. This shows the importance of continuity in litigation.

Key Terms
خصم (khasm): Litigant; one who can be sued or can sue in the same case.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate, the maximum for bequests when there are heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario from al-Jami', why does the judge make the first legatee a litigant for the second legatee?
A) Because the first legatee inherited the property.
B) Because the first legatee holds property that is part of the same bequest fund.
C) Because the first legatee is an heir.
D) Because the judge wants to punish the first legatee.

Key Takeaway
When two legatees each prove a bequest of one-third, they share the one-third fund equally, and the first must pay the second half of what he received; if insolvent, the second may recover from the heir's share at a reduced rate.

Dispute on Defining 'Relatives' in Bequests
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of 'relatives' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's definitions of 'relatives' in a bequest and apply the later practical ruling to a modern scenario.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa limits 'relatives' to nearest mahram; the Sahibayn include all to furthest Muslim ancestor — the practical ruling narrows it due to abundance.

When a testator bequeaths 'to my relatives,' the Hanafi school has a significant internal disagreement. This passage from Bahr al-Raiq presents the views of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, along with the linguistic and analogical proofs. Understanding this dispute is key to correctly implementing such bequests, especially as the practical ruling has been refined over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the operative phrase
The testator says 'to my relatives' (aqarib). What is the legal issue? The term is ambiguous and the testator's intent must be interpreted.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa: nearest mahram relative, at least two, excluding parents and children. Sahibayn: all relatives to the furthest Muslim ancestor, including non-mahram.
Both agree that the bequest is for two or more.
3
Trace the dalil of each
Abu Hanifa uses qiyas with inheritance (nearest inherits) and the purpose of silat ar-rahim (obligatory only for mahram). Sahibayn use linguistic generality of 'qarib'.
The Quranic verse (2:180) conjoining 'parents' and 'relatives' supports Abu Hanifa's exclusion.
4
Apply the ikhtilaf to a hypothetical
For a bequest to the Prophet's relatives: Sahibayn include children of Abu Talib (if attaining Islam); Abu Hanifa limits to mahram (e.g., children of Ali).
This shows the practical impact.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and later practice
Later scholars limited distribution due to abundance: restrict to children of father, grandfather, great-grandfather, and mother's side equivalents, excluding further degrees.
This is the operative ruling today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وجنسه أهل بيت أبيه) لأن الانسان بأبيه فصار كأنه يتجنس قرابته حيث يدخل فيه جهة الأب والأم لأن الكل يسمون قرابته فلا يختص بشيء منهم، وكذا أهل نسبته وأهل نسبه فيكون حكمه حكم جميع ما ذكرنا ويدخل فيه الأب والجد لأن الأب أصل النسب والجد أصل نسب أبيه. وقال في الكافي : لو كان الأب الأكبر حياً لا يدخل تحت الوصية لأن الوصية للمضاف لا للمضاف إليه، ولو أوصت المرأة لجنسها أو لأهل بيتها لا يدخل ولدها لأن ولدها ينسب إلى أبيه لا إليها إلا أن يكون أبوه من قوم أبيها وقرابته. قال رحمه الله : ( وإن أوصى لأقاربه أو لذوي قرابته أو لأرحامه أو لأنسابه) فهي للأقرب فالأقرب . رب من كل ذي رحم محرم منه ولا يدخل الوالدان والولد والوارث ويكون للاثنين فصاعداً. وهذا عند أبي حنيفة. وقالا : الوصية لكل من ينسب إلى أقصى أب له في الاسلام وإن لم يسلم بعد أن أدرك الاسلام أو أسلم على ما اختلف فيه المشايخ، وفائدة الاختلاف تظهر في مثل أبي طالب وعلي رضي الله عنه إذا وقعت الوصية لأقرباء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يدخل فيه أولاد أبي طالب وعلى هذا وقعت الوصية على قول من شرط الاسلام ويدخلون على قول من شرط أدراك الاسلام ومن شرط إسلامه صرفه إلى أولاد علي لا غير، ولا يدخل أولاد عبد المطلب بالإجماع لأنه لم يدرك الاسلام. لهما أن الاسم يتناول الكل لأن لفظة القريب حقيقة للكل إذ هي مشتقة من القرابة فيكون اسماً لكل من قامت به . فيتناول مواضع الخلاف ضرورة. ولأبي حنيفة أن الوصية أخت الميراث وفي الميراث يعتبر من الأقرب فالأقرب فكذا في أخته لأن الأخت لا تخالف الأخت في الأحكام، ولأن المقصود هذه الوصية تلافي ما فرط في إقامة الواجب وهو صلة الرحم والوجوب يختص بذي الرحم المحرم ولا معتبر بظاهر اللفظ بعد انعقاد الإجماع على تركه فإن كلا منهما قيده بما ذكره، والإمام الشافعي قيده بالأب الأدنى. ولا تدخل قرابة الأولاد عندنا لأنهم لا يسمون أقرباء عادة ومن يسمى والده قريباً يكون منه عقوقاً إذ القريب في عرف أهل اللغة من تقرب إلى غيره بواسطة غيره، وتقرب الوالد والولد بنفسه لا بغيره ولهذا عطف القريب على الوالدين في قوله تعالى : الوصية للوالدين والأقربين ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٠] والعطف للمغايرة، ولو كان منهم لما عطفوا عليهما. ويدخل فيه الجد والجدة وولد الولد في ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أنهم لا يدخلون، وقيل ما ذكراه إلى أنه يصرف إلى أقصى أب له في الاسلام كان في ذلك الزمان حين لم يكن في أقرباء الانسان الذين ينسبون إلى أقصى أب له في الاسلام كثرة، وأما في زماننا ففيهم كثرة لا يمكن احصاؤهم فيصرف الوصية إلى أولاد أبيه وجده وجد أبيه وأولاد أمه وجد أمه وجدته وجده ،أمه ولا يصرف إلى أكثر من ذلك . ويستوي الحر والعبد والمسلم والكافر، والصغير والكبير والذكر والأنثى على المذهبين. وإنما يكون للاثنين فصاعداً عنده لأن المذكور فيه بلفظ الجمع وفي الميراث يراد بالجمع المثنى فكذا في الوصية لأنها أخته. قال الراجي عفو ربه : هذا ظاهر في الأقارب، وأما في الانسان فمشكل لأنه جمع نسب وفيه لا تدخل قرابته من جهة الأم فكيف دخلوا فيه هنا؟
He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And his kin [jins] are the people of his father's house) because a person is [identified] by his father, so it becomes as if his kinship is categorized by it, since it includes the father's side and the mother's side because all are called his relatives, so it is not restricted to any one of them. Similarly, his [family of] lineage and his lineage, so its ruling is the ruling of all that we mentioned, and it includes the father and the grandfather because the father is the origin of lineage and the grandfather is the origin of his father's lineage. And it is said in al-Kafi: If the great-grandfather is alive, he does not fall under the bequest because the bequest is for the adjunct, not the object of the adjunct. And if a woman makes a bequest to her jins or to her household, her child does not enter because her child is attributed to his father, not to her, unless his father is from the people of her father and his relatives. He, may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if he makes a bequest to his relatives or to his kin or to his kinsmen or to his relations) then it is for the nearest and nearer. [It is] for every mahram relative from him, and parents and children and the heir are not included, and it is for two or more. And this is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two [disciples] said: The bequest is for everyone who is related to his furthest ancestor in Islam, even if he did not become Muslim after having attained Islam or became Muslim, as the masters differed on it. And the benefit of the difference appears in the case of Abu Talib and Ali, may Allah be pleased with him: if the bequest is made to the relatives of the Prophet, peace be upon him, the children of Abu Talib are not included according to the one who stipulated Islam, and they are included according to the one who stipulated attaining Islam, and according to the one who stipulated his Islam, it is restricted to the children of Ali only. And the children of Abdul Muttalib are not included by consensus because he did not attain Islam. Their proof is that the name includes all because the word 'qarib' is true for all, as it is derived from 'qarabah', so it becomes a name for everyone who has [that] relationship. So it necessarily includes the points of disagreement. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that the bequest is the sister of inheritance, and in inheritance the nearest and nearer are considered, so also in its sister, because the sister does not contradict the sister in rulings. And because the purpose of this bequest is to make up for what was neglected in performing the duty, which is maintaining ties of kinship, and the obligation is specific to the mahram relative, and the outward wording is not considered after the consensus to abandon it, for each of them restricted it with what he mentioned. And Imam al-Shafi'i restricted it to the nearest father. And the relatives of children are not included according to us because they are not usually called relatives, and whoever calls his father a relative would be undutiful, because 'relative' in the usage of the language is one who is related to another through another, and the closeness of the parent and child is by themselves not through another. For this reason, 'relative' is conjoined to 'parents' in His statement: 'The bequest is for parents and near relatives' [2:180], and conjunction implies difference. And if they were from among them, they would not have been conjoined to them. And the grandfather, grandmother, and grandchild are included in the apparent riwayah, and from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that they are not included. And it is said that what they mentioned is that it is to be given to the furthest ancestor in Islam. That was in that time when there were not many relatives of a person who are related to the furthest ancestor in Islam. As for our time, there are many, impossible to count, so the bequest is to be given to the children of his father, his grandfather, the grandfather of his father, and the children of his mother, the grandfather of his mother, his grandmother, and the grandfather of his mother, and not to more than that. And free and slave, Muslim and disbeliever, minor and adult, male and female are equal on the two madhhabs. And it is only for two or more according to him because it is mentioned in the plural form, and in inheritance the plural means two, so also in bequest because it is its sister. The one hoping for his Lord's pardon said: This is apparent regarding relatives. As for 'insan' [human], it is problematic because it is a plural of lineage and in it the relatives from the mother's side are not included, so how are they included here?
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab and inter-madhhab dispute about the scope of a bequest to relatives. It begins by commenting on the matn phrase 'and his kin (jins) are the people of his father's house', explaining that a person is identified by his father, so his kinship includes both paternal and maternal sides equally. However, it notes an exception from al-Kafi: if the great-grandfather is alive, he is not included because the bequest is for the adjunct (e.g., 'descendants'), not the ancestor himself. For a woman, her children are not included unless the father is from her own paternal clan. The main dispute centers on the interpretation of 'to his relatives' (aqarib). Abu Hanifa holds that it goes to the nearest mahram relative (excluding parents and children), with at least two recipients. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it includes all descendants of the furthest ancestor who embraced Islam, regardless of mahram status. The practical difference appears in bequests to the Prophet's relatives: whether children of Abu Talib (who did not embrace Islam) are included. The disciples argue that the word 'qarib' linguistically includes all blood relations. Abu Hanifa uses qiyas to inheritance, where only the nearest relative inherits, and stresses the purpose of maintaining ties with mahram relatives. The passage also mentions Imam al-Shafi'i's view, which restricts it to the nearest father (i.e., only direct paternal line). The contemporary practice in the commentators' time, due to the difficulty of counting, is to limit the distribution to a certain circle: children of father, grandfather, great-grandfather, and likewise on mother's side. The commentator ('al-rajī 'afwa rabbih') raises a problem: the phrase 'aqarib' normally excludes maternal relatives, yet here they are included? This is left unresolved. The key takeaway is that the default ruling for a bequest to 'relatives' is disputed within the Hanafi school, with the Sahibayn's broader definition being applied in a limited fashion in practice.

Key Terms
جنس (jins): Kin, category; used in the matn to mean 'his kind' or 'his kin', i.e., the people of his father's house.
أقصى أب له في الإسلام (aqsa ab lahu fi al-Islam): The furthest ancestor of the testator who embraced Islam (or at least attained the time of Islam).
محرم (mahram): A blood relative permanently prohibited from marriage (e.g., sister, niece, aunt, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to Abu Hanifa, what is the minimum number of recipients for a bequest to 'relatives'?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Any number

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on the scope of 'relatives' in a bequest, but the operative ruling restricts distribution to a manageable circle due to practical difficulty.

intermediate
8 min
Defining 'Aqarib': Who Enters a Bequest to Relatives?
Defining the scope of 'aqarib' in bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'aqarib' (relatives) for bequests and explain why parents and children are excluded, using the Quranic conjunction as evidence.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'aqarib' excludes parents and children — the Quranic conjunction proves they are distinct categories.

When a testator bequeaths to 'aqarib' (relatives), who exactly qualifies? The Hanafi school draws a sharp line: parents and children are not 'aqarib'. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and scriptural reasoning behind that exclusion, and explains which blood relatives do enter (e.g., grandparents, grandchildren).

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic argument
The sharh explains that in Arabic, a 'relative' (qarib) is someone connected through an intermediary, while parents and children are directly related. Therefore, calling them 'aqarib' would be linguistically improper.
This is a key linguistic analysis that shapes the legal scope.
2
Examine the Quranic proof (2:180)
The verse 'al-wasiyyatu lil-walidayni wal-aqrabin' conjoins 'walidayn' (parents) and 'aqrabin' (relatives). Conjunction (athf) implies difference — thus 'aqrabin' cannot include parents or children.
Hanafi usul: al-athf yuqtaḍī al-mughāyarah.
3
Explore the inclusion of grandparents and grandchildren
The text states that in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), grandparents and grandchildren enter under 'aqarib'. There is also a minority narration excluding them.
This illustrates the spectrum of Hanafi positions even on basic definitions.
4
Note the condition of mahram
Abu Hanifa requires that at least one mahram relative exist for the bequest to be valid. If no mahram is present, the bequest is void according to him.
The Sahibayn differ — they do not require mahram for validity.

كتاب الوصايا/ باب الوصية للأقارب وغيرهم
من الأقرب فالأقرب فكذا في أخته لأن الأخت لا تخالف الأخت في الأحكام، ولأن المقصود هذه الوصية تلافي ما فرط في إقامة الواجب وهو صلة الرحم والوجوب يختص بذي الرحم المحرم ولا معتبر بظاهر اللفظ بعد انعقاد الإجماع على تركه فإن كلا منهما قيده بما ذكره، والإمام الشافعي قيده بالأب الأدنى. ولا تدخل قرابة الأولاد عندنا لأنهم لا يسمون أقرباء عادة ومن يسمى والده قريباً يكون منه عقوقاً إذ القريب في عرف أهل اللغة من تقرب إلى غيره بواسطة غيره، وتقرب الوالد والولد بنفسه لا بغيره ولهذا عطف القريب على الوالدين في قوله تعالى : الوصية للوالدين والأقربين ﴾ [البقرة : ١٨٠] والعطف للمغايرة، ولو كان منهم لما عطفوا عليهما. ويدخل فيه الجد والجدة وولد الولد في ظاهر الرواية، وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف أنهم لا يدخلون، وقيل ما ذكراه إلى أنه يصرف إلى أقصى أب له في الاسلام كان في ذلك الزمان حين لم يكن في أقرباء الانسان الذين ينسبون إلى أقصى أب له في الاسلام كثرة، وأما في زماننا ففيهم كثرة لا يمكن احصاؤهم فيصرف الوصية إلى أولاد أبيه وجده وجد أبيه وأولاد أمه وجد أمه وجدته وجده ،أمه ولا يصرف إلى أكثر من ذلك . ويستوي الحر والعبد والمسلم والكافر، والصغير والكبير والذكر والأنثى على المذهبين. وإنما يكون للاثنين فصاعداً عنده لأن المذكور فيه بلفظ الجمع وفي الميراث يراد بالجمع المثنى فكذا في الوصية لأنها أخته. قال الراجي عفو ربه : هذا ظاهر في الأقارب، وأما في الانسان فمشكل لأنه جمع نسب وفيه لا تدخل قرابته من جهة الأم فكيف دخلوا فيه هنا؟ قال في الأصل: ولو ترك الموصي ولداً يحوز ميراثه وترك عمين وخالين فالوصية عند أبي حنيفة للعمين، وإنما شرط قيام الولد كيلا يكون العمان وارثين وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد الوصية بين العمين والخالين أرباعاً لاستوائهم في تناول اسم القريب، ولو كان عماً وخالين فللعم النصف والباقي للخالين عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما الوصية بينهم بالسوية. وإن ترك عماً وعمة وخالاً وخالة فالوصية للعم والعمة عند أبي حنيفة. وفي الكافي : ولو أوصى لأقاربه وله عمان وخالان فالوصية لعميه عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يقسم بينهم أرباعاً، وكذا في قوله لأرحامه ولذوي أرحامه ولأنسابه ولذوي أنسابه ولو قال لذوي قرابته أو لذي نسبته أو لقرابته فالجواب ما ذكرنا إذ هنا لا يعتبر الجمع عند أبي حنيفة فإنه يدخل تحت الوصية الأقرب فالأقرب والواحد فصاعداً بلا خلاف. وفي الكافي ولو أوصى لذوي قرابته لا يشترط فيه الجمع لاستحقاق الكل حتى لو كان له وخالان فكله للعم عنده . قال : ويعتبر في هذه المسائل قرابة الموصى له وقت موت الموصي لا وقت الإيصاء. قال في الأصل: وإن لم يكن ذو رحم في هذه المسائل فالوصية باطلة عند أبي حنيفة. وفي النوازل وفي الظهيرية : الوصية إذا كانوا إلا يحصون اختلف المشايخ في جوازها قال بعضهم : إنها باطلة . وقال محمد بن سلمة : إنها جائزة وعليه الفتوى لأنها قرية لكونها صلة. ولو أوصى بثلث ماله للموصي
النصف ولهما النصف ولو له عم وعمة استويا ولولد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء ولورثة لأهل بيته دخل في الوصية كل من يتصل به من قبل آبائه إلى اقصى أب له في الاسلام يستوي فيه المسلم والكافر والذكر والأنثى، والمحرم والقريب والبعيد. ونسب الإنسان من قبل أبيه وكل من يتصل به من قبل آبائه إلى أقصى أب في الإسلام فهو من أهل بيت نسبته فيدخل تحت الوصية ولا يدخل تحت الوصية أولاد البنات قال : إلا إذا كان أزواجهن من بني أعمام الوصي وعشيرته، ولا يدخل فيه أولاد الأخوات ولا أحد من قرابة أم الموصي . وإذا أوصى الجنسه فهذا وما لو أوصى لأهل بيته سواء لأن الانسان من جنس قوام ابيه ألا ترى أن إبراهيم ولد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان قريشاً وكذلك أولاد الخلفاء يصلحون للخلافة وإن كان أكثرهم من الإماء واعتبروا من جنس قوم آبائهم فصار قوله وجنسه وقوله لأهل بيته سواء وكل من يتصل به إلى اقصى أب في الاسلام يدخل تحت الوصية إن أوصى لآله فهذا وما لو أوصى لأهل بيته سواء لأنهم يستعملون استعمالاً واحداً يقال آل محمد وأهل بيت محمد وآل عباس وأهل بيت عباس. إذا اوصى بثلث ماله لأهله أو لأهل فلان فالوصية للزوجة خاصة دون من سواها قياساً إلا أنا استحسنا وجعلنا الوصية لكل من يكون عياله وتلزمه نفقتهم ويضمهم بيته ولا يدخل تحت الوصية مماليكه فلو كان أهل في بلدتين أو في بيتين دخلوا تحت الوصية لعموم اللفظ .
قال رحمه الله : (فإن كان له عمان وخالان فهي لعميه لأنهما أقرب كما في الأرث ولفظ الجمع يراد به المثنى في الوصية على ما بينا فكذا هنا وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما يكون بينهم أرباعاً لأنهم لا يعتبرون الأقرب وقد تقدم قال رحمه الله (ولو كان له عم وخالان كان له النصف ولهما النصف) أي لو كان له وخالان كان للعم نصف ما أوصى به وللخالين النصف لأن اللفظ جمع فلا بد من اعتبار معنى الجمع فيه وهو الإتيان في الوصية على ما عرف فيضم إلى العم الخالان ليصير جمعاً فيأخذ هو النصف لأنه أقرب ويأخذان النصف بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لذي قرابته حيث يكون جميع اعتبار الوصية للعم إذ هو الأقرب، ولو كان له واحد لا غير كان له نصف الوصية لما بينا أنه لا بد من اعتبار الجمع فيه ويرد النصف إلى الورثة لعدم من يستحقه لأن اللفظ جمع وأدناه اثنان في الوصية فيكون لكل واحد منهما النصف والنصف الآخر يرد إلى الورثة قال رحمه الله : (ولو له عم وعمة استويا) لأن قرابتهما مستويان ومعنى الجمع قد تحقق بهما فاستحقا حتى لو كان له أخوال معهما لا يستحقون شيئاً لأنهما أقرب ولا حاجة إلى الضم إليهما لكمال النصاب بهما، ولو انعدم المحرم بطلت الوصية لأنها متقيدة بهذا فلا بد من مراعاته، وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة . وعندهما لا تبطل ولا تختص الأعمام بالوصية دون الأخوال لما عرف من مذهبهما وقدمنا بیانه . قال رحمه الله : (ولولد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء) يعني لو أوصى لأولاد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء
Book of Bequests / Chapter of Bequest to Relatives and Others. From the nearest then the nearest, likewise for his sister, because the sister does not differ from the sister in rulings, and because the purpose of this bequest is to make up for what was neglected in performing the obligation, which is maintaining family ties, and the obligation is specific to a mahram relative, and no consideration is given to the literal wording after consensus has been reached on abandoning it, for each of them restricted it by what he mentioned. Imam al-Shafi'i restricted it to the nearer father. The kinship of children does not enter according to us because they are not usually called relatives, and whoever calls his father a relative would be acting disrespectfully, for 'relative' in the linguistic custom of the people is one who becomes close to another through an intermediary, while the closeness of a parent and child is by themselves without an intermediary; therefore 'relative' is conjoined with parents in His statement: 'Bequest is for parents and relatives' (al-Baqarah 2:180), and conjunction indicates difference; had they been among them, they would not have been conjoined to them. The grandfather, grandmother, and child's child enter in the apparent narration, and from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that they do not enter. It was said what they both mentioned: that it is directed to the farthest father in Islam. That was at that time when there were not many relatives of a person who trace back to the farthest father in Islam. As for our time, there are so many that they cannot be counted, so the bequest is directed to the children of his father, his grandfather, his great-grandfather, the children of his mother, her grandfather, her grandmother, and his maternal grandfather, and not beyond that. The free and the slave, the Muslim and the disbeliever, the young and the old, the male and the female are equal according to both schools. It is only for two or more according to him because what is mentioned is in a plural form, and in inheritance the plural intends the dual; similarly in bequest because it is its sister. The one hoping for his Lord's forgiveness said: This is clear regarding relatives, but regarding 'the person' it is problematic because it is a collective noun of lineage, and in it the relative from the mother's side does not enter, so how did they enter here? He said in al-Asl: If the testator left a child who inherits from him, and left two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest according to Abu Hanifa is for the two paternal uncles; he only stipulated the existence of a child so that the two paternal uncles would not be heirs. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the bequest is divided between the two paternal uncles and the two maternal uncles in quarters because they are equal in being encompassed by the term 'relative'. If there were a paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle half and the rest for the two maternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, the bequest is divided equally among them. If he left a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, the bequest is for the paternal uncle and paternal aunt according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Kafi: If he made a bequest to his relatives and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, it is divided between them in quarters. Similarly in his saying: to his close relatives, and to his uterine relatives, and to his lineages, and to his blood relatives. If he said: to his near relations or to his relative or to his relationship, the answer is what we mentioned, for here plurality is not considered according to Abu Hanifa, for the nearest then nearest enters the bequest, and one or more, without dispute. In al-Kafi: If he bequeathed to his near relations, plurality is not required for entitlement of all; even if he had a paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, all goes to the paternal uncle according to him. He said: In these matters, consideration is given to the relationship of the legatee at the time of the testator's death, not at the time of bequest. He said in al-Asl: If there is no mahram relative in these matters, the bequest is void according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Nawazil and al-Zahiriyya: If the relatives are too numerous to count, the scholars differed on the permissibility of the bequest; some said it is void. Muhammad ibn Salama said it is permissible and the fatwa is upon it because it is a kindness as it is a connection. If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the testator... half and for them half; if he has a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt, they are equal; and to the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal; and to the heirs of his household, included in the bequest is everyone connected to him through his fathers up to the farthest father in Islam; the Muslim and disbeliever, male and female, mahram and non-mahram, near and distant are equal. A person's lineage is from his father's side, and everyone connected to him through his fathers up to the farthest father in Islam is from his household by lineage, so he enters under the bequest. The daughters' children do not enter under the bequest unless their husbands are from the testator's paternal cousins and tribe. The children of sisters do not enter, nor anyone from the mother's relatives of the testator. If he bequeaths to his kind, this is the same as if he bequeaths to his household, because a person is from the kind of his father's people; do you not see that Ibrahim, the son of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), was a Quraysh, and likewise the children of the caliphs are fit for the caliphate even if most of them were from slave women, and they are considered from the kind of their fathers' people. So his saying 'his kind' and his saying 'to his household' are the same. Everyone connected to him up to the farthest father in Islam enters under the bequest if he bequeaths to his family; this is the same as if he bequeaths to his household because they are used interchangeably; one says the family of Muhammad and the household of Muhammad, the family of Abbas and the household of Abbas. If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to his family or to the household of so-and-so, the bequest is for the wife specifically, to the exclusion of others, by analogy, except that we applied istihsan and made the bequest for everyone who is his dependent, whose maintenance is obligatory upon him, and whom his house encompasses. His slaves do not enter under the bequest. If the family were in two towns or in two houses, they enter under the bequest due to the generality of the wording.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then it is for his two paternal uncles because they are closer, as in inheritance, and the plural form is used to mean the dual in bequest as we explained; so similarly here. This is according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, it is divided between them in quarters because they do not consider the closer relative. And it has preceded.) He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has a paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for him half and for them half), meaning if he has (a paternal uncle) and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half of what he bequeathed, and for the two maternal uncles the other half, because the wording is plural, so consideration of the meaning of plurality is necessary, which is to bring about the bequest as known; so the paternal uncle is joined with the maternal uncles to form a plural, so he takes half because he is closer, and they take half. Unlike if he bequeaths to his near relation, where all consideration of the bequest is for the paternal uncle since he is the closest. If he has only one relative, he gets half the bequest because we have stated that plurality must be considered, and the other half is returned to the heirs due to the lack of someone entitled to it, because the wording is plural and its minimum is two in bequest, so each gets half and the other half is returned to the heirs. He said: (If he has a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt, they are equal) because their relation is equal and the meaning of plurality is achieved by them, so they are entitled. Even if there are maternal uncles with them, they do not get anything because they are closer, and there is no need to join them because the quorum is complete with them. If the mahram relative is absent, the bequest is void because it is restricted to this condition, so it must be observed. All this according to Abu Hanifa. According to them, it is not void, nor are paternal uncles singled out for the bequest to the exclusion of maternal uncles, due to what is known of their school, and we have already explained it. He said: (And to the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal), meaning if he bequeaths to the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explaining the rulings on bequests to relatives and other categories. It begins by establishing the principle that a bequest to 'aqarib' (relatives) goes to the nearest then the nearest, akin to inheritance. The author clarifies that the term 'aqarib' does not include parents or children, as they are not commonly called 'aqarib' in linguistic usage; rather, the Quranic verse (2:180) distinguishes between 'parents' and 'relatives' by conjunction, indicating mutual exclusivity. Grandparents and grandchildren are included in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), though a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf excludes them, directing the bequest to the farthest ancestor in Islam. The text then discusses the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the distribution when multiple relatives of different degrees exist. Abu Hanifa holds that the nearest relative takes the entire bequest, while the Sahibayn divide it equally among all relatives who fall under the term. The passage also explores the requirement of plurality: when the testator says 'to my relatives' (li-aqaribi), the plural form necessitates at least two recipients; if only one relative exists, half goes to that relative and half returns to the testator's heirs. Specific examples are given: with two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa gives the bequest to the paternal uncles (as they are closer), while the Sahibayn divide it into quarters among all four. With one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa gives half to the paternal uncle and half to the maternal uncles; the Sahibayn divide equally. The bequest is valid only if there is a mahram relative; otherwise, Abu Hanifa deems it void, while the Sahibayn uphold validity. The passage then addresses bequests to 'ahl baytihi' (his household), 'jinsihi' (his kind), and 'alihi' (his family). These terms are treated similarly, referring to all individuals connected to the testator through his paternal lineage up to the farthest Muslim ancestor, excluding children of daughters (unless their husbands are from the testator's paternal cousins) and relatives on the mother's side. A bequest to 'ahlihi' or 'ahl fulan' is, by analogy, limited to the wife, but istihsan expands it to all dependents whose maintenance is obligatory and who live with him. The passage concludes with the matn recapitulating the cases: the ruling for two paternal and two maternal uncles, one paternal and two maternal uncles, a paternal uncle and aunt, and children of so-and-so (where male and female are equal). Throughout, Abu Hanifa's positions are contrasted with those of the Sahibayn, with the text clearly stating the relied-upon view where applicable.

Key Terms
الأقارب (al-aqarib): Relatives by blood; in this context, specifically those who are not parents or children, and according to Abu Hanifa includes only paternal relatives up to the farthest ancestor in Islam, excluding maternal side.
المحرم (al-mahram): A relative whom one cannot marry due to blood relation (e.g., father, mother, brother, sister). In this passage, the bequest to relatives is only valid if there is a mahram relative among them; otherwise it is void according to Abu Hanifa.
العطف (al-athf): Grammatical conjunction; in this passage, the conjunction of 'aqarib' with 'parents' in the Quran is used as evidence that they are separate categories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT included in the term 'aqarib' for bequest purposes?
A) A paternal uncle
B) A maternal aunt
C) A granddaughter
D) A father

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, 'aqarib' for bequests excludes parents and children, and in the apparent narration, includes grandparents and grandchildren, with the bequest directed to the nearest paternal relatives.

intermediate
10 min
Distributing a Bequest Among Relatives: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the distribution of a bequest to relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Abu Hanifa's rule of 'al-aqrab fa al-aqrab' and the Sahibayn's equal division rule to concrete cases of bequests to relatives, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When bequeathing to relatives, Abu Hanifa gives all to the nearest; the Sahibayn divide equally among all relatives of equal degree.

The previous lesson defined who counts as 'aqarib'. Now we tackle a key dispute: if the testator has multiple relatives of different degrees (e.g., paternal uncles and maternal uncles), should the bequest go only to the nearest, or be shared among all? Abu Hanifa and his two chief disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, gave opposing answers. This lesson walks through the concrete examples in the text to see how each rule works and which view is ultimately relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the core dispute
Abu Hanifa applies inheritance's 'closer relative takes all' principle to bequests. The Sahibayn treat all relatives qualifying as 'aqarib' equally, dividing the bequest among them proportionally.
The dispute is about whether proximity in degree matters.
2
Analyze the first example: two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles
Under Abu Hanifa, the two paternal uncles (closer) take the whole bequest. Under the Sahibayn, all four divide equally, each getting one quarter.
This is the most cited example in the passage.
3
Analyze the second example: one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles
Abu Hanifa gives half to the paternal uncle (closer) and half to the maternal uncles (because plurality requires at least two; the maternal uncles are two, so they get half). Under the Sahibayn, all three divide equally into thirds.
The half/half result under Abu Hanifa accounts for the plural form requirement.
4
Consider the case of only one relative
If only one relative exists (e.g., one paternal uncle), Abu Hanifa gives him half the bequest (because 'aqarib' is plural requiring at least two), and the other half returns to the heirs. The Sahibayn would give him the entire bequest.
The plural requirement is unique to Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Check the mufta bihi position
The text notes that the fatwa is upon Muhammad ibn Salama's view when relatives are too numerous. For the main dispute, later Hanafi practice often adopts the Sahibayn's view as it is more inclusive and easier to apply.
Tarjih authority: Al-Bahr al-Raiq mentions 'wa al-fatwa alaan 'ala qawl Muhammad ibn Salama' for the case of numerous relatives.

من الأقرب فالأقرب فكذا في أخته لأن الأخت لا تخالف الأخت في الأحكام، ولأن المقصود هذه الوصية تلافي ما فرط في إقامة الواجب وهو صلة الرحم والوجوب يختص بذي الرحم المحرم ولا معتبر بظاهر اللفظ بعد انعقاد الحر والعبد والمسلم والكافر، والصغير والكبير والذكر والأنثى على المذهبين. وإنما يكون للاثنين فصاعداً عنده لأن المذكور فيه بلفظ الجمع وفي الميراث يراد بالجمع المثنى فكذا في الوصية لأنها أخته. قال أبي حنيفة للعمين، وإنما شرط قيام الولد كيلا يكون العمان وارثين وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد الوصية بين العمين والخالين أرباعاً لاستوائهم في تناول اسم القريب، ولو كان عماً وخالين فللعم النصف والباقي للخالين عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما الوصية بينهم بالسوية. وإن ترك عماً وعمة وخالاً وخالة فالوصية للعم والعمة عند أبي حنيفة. وفي الكافي : ولو أوصى لأقاربه وله عمان وخالان فالوصية لعميه عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما يقسم بينهم أرباعاً، وكذا في قوله لأرحامه ولذوي أرحامه ولأنسابه ولذوي أنسابه ولو قال لذوي قرابته أو لذي نسبته أو لقرابته فالجواب ما ذكرنا إذ هنا لا يعتبر الجمع عند أبي حنيفة فإنه يدخل تحت الوصية الأقرب فالأقرب والواحد فصاعداً بلا خلاف. وفي الكافي ولو أوصى لذوي قرابته لا يشترط فيه الجمع لاستحقاق الكل حتى لو كان له وخالان فكله للعم عنده . قال : ويعتبر في هذه المسائل قرابة الموصى له وقت موت الموصي لا وقت الإيصاء. قال في الأصل: وإن لم يكن ذو رحم في هذه المسائل فالوصية باطلة عند أبي حنيفة. وفي النوازل وفي الظهيرية : الوصية إذا كانوا إلا يحصون اختلف المشايخ في جوازها قال بعضهم : إنها باطلة . وقال محمد بن سلمة : إنها جائزة وعليه الفتوى لأنها قرية لكونها صلة. ولو أوصى بثلث ماله للموصي
النصف ولهما النصف ولو له عم وعمة استويا ولولد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء ولورثة لأهل بيته دخل في الوصية كل من يتصل به من قبل آبائه إلى اقصى أب له في الاسلام يستوي فيه المسلم والكافر والذكر والأنثى، والمحرم والقريب والبعيد. ونسب الإنسان من قبل أبيه وكل من يتصل به من قبل آبائه إلى أقصى أب في الإسلام فهو من أهل بيت نسبته فيدخل تحت الوصية ولا يدخل تحت الوصية أولاد البنات قال : إلا إذا كان أزواجهن من بني أعمام الوصي وعشيرته، ولا يدخل فيه أولاد الأخوات ولا أحد من قرابة أم الموصي . وإذا أوصى الجنسه فهذا وما لو أوصى لأهل بيته سواء لأن الانسان من جنس قوام ابيه ألا ترى أن إبراهيم ولد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كان قريشاً وكذلك أولاد الخلفاء يصلحون للخلافة وإن كان أكثرهم من الإماء واعتبروا من جنس قوم آبائهم فصار قوله وجنسه وقوله لأهل بيته سواء وكل من يتصل به إلى اقصى أب في الاسلام يدخل تحت الوصية إن أوصى لآله فهذا وما لو أوصى لأهل بيته سواء لأنهم يستعملون استعمالاً واحداً يقال آل محمد وأهل بيت محمد وآل عباس وأهل بيت عباس. إذا اوصى بثلث ماله لأهله أو لأهل فلان فالوصية للزوجة خاصة دون من سواها قياساً إلا أنا استحسنا وجعلنا الوصية لكل من يكون عياله وتلزمه نفقتهم ويضمهم بيته ولا يدخل تحت الوصية مماليكه فلو كان أهل في بلدتين أو في بيتين دخلوا تحت الوصية لعموم اللفظ .
قال رحمه الله : (فإن كان له عمان وخالان فهي لعميه لأنهما أقرب كما في الأرث ولفظ الجمع يراد به المثنى في الوصية على ما بينا فكذا هنا وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما يكون بينهم أرباعاً لأنهم لا يعتبرون الأقرب وقد تقدم قال رحمه الله (ولو كان له عم وخالان كان له النصف ولهما النصف) أي لو كان له وخالان كان للعم نصف ما أوصى به وللخالين النصف لأن اللفظ جمع فلا بد من اعتبار معنى الجمع فيه وهو الإتيان في الوصية على ما عرف فيضم إلى العم الخالان ليصير جمعاً فيأخذ هو النصف لأنه أقرب ويأخذان النصف بخلاف ما إذا أوصى لذي قرابته حيث يكون جميع اعتبار الوصية للعم إذ هو الأقرب، ولو كان له واحد لا غير كان له نصف الوصية لما بينا أنه لا بد من اعتبار الجمع فيه ويرد النصف إلى الورثة لعدم من يستحقه لأن اللفظ جمع وأدناه اثنان في الوصية فيكون لكل واحد منهما النصف والنصف الآخر يرد إلى الورثة قال رحمه الله : (ولو له عم وعمة استويا) لأن قرابتهما مستويان ومعنى الجمع قد تحقق بهما فاستحقا حتى لو كان له أخوال معهما لا يستحقون شيئاً لأنهما أقرب ولا حاجة إلى الضم إليهما لكمال النصاب بهما، ولو انعدم المحرم بطلت الوصية لأنها متقيدة بهذا فلا بد من مراعاته، وهذا كله عند أبي حنيفة . وعندهما لا تبطل ولا تختص الأعمام بالوصية دون الأخوال لما عرف من مذهبهما وقدمنا بیانه . قال رحمه الله : (ولولد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء) يعني لو أوصى لأولاد فلان للذكر والأنثى سواء
Book of Bequests / Chapter of Bequest to Relatives and Others. From the nearest then the nearest, likewise for his sister, because the sister does not differ from the sister in rulings, and because the purpose of this bequest is to make up for what was neglected in performing the obligation, which is maintaining family ties, and the obligation is specific to a mahram relative, and no consideration is given to the literal wording after consensus has been reached on abandoning it, for each of them restricted it by what he mentioned. Imam al-Shafi'i restricted it to the nearer father. The kinship of children does not enter according to us because they are not usually called relatives, and whoever calls his father a relative would be acting disrespectfully, for 'relative' in the linguistic custom of the people is one who becomes close to another through an intermediary, while the closeness of a parent and child is by themselves without an intermediary; therefore 'relative' is conjoined with parents in His statement: 'Bequest is for parents and relatives' (al-Baqarah 2:180), and conjunction indicates difference; had they been among them, they would not have been conjoined to them. The grandfather, grandmother, and child's child enter in the apparent narration, and from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that they do not enter. It was said what they both mentioned: that it is directed to the farthest father in Islam. That was at that time when there were not many relatives of a person who trace back to the farthest father in Islam. As for our time, there are so many that they cannot be counted, so the bequest is directed to the children of his father, his grandfather, his great-grandfather, the children of his mother, her grandfather, her grandmother, and his maternal grandfather, and not beyond that. The free and the slave, the Muslim and the disbeliever, the young and the old, the male and the female are equal according to both schools. It is only for two or more according to him because what is mentioned is in a plural form, and in inheritance the plural intends the dual; similarly in bequest because it is its sister. The one hoping for his Lord's forgiveness said: This is clear regarding relatives, but regarding 'the person' it is problematic because it is a collective noun of lineage, and in it the relative from the mother's side does not enter, so how did they enter here? He said in al-Asl: If the testator left a child who inherits from him, and left two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest according to Abu Hanifa is for the two paternal uncles; he only stipulated the existence of a child so that the two paternal uncles would not be heirs. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the bequest is divided between the two paternal uncles and the two maternal uncles in quarters because they are equal in being encompassed by the term 'relative'. If there were a paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle half and the rest for the two maternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, the bequest is divided equally among them. If he left a paternal uncle, a paternal aunt, a maternal uncle, and a maternal aunt, the bequest is for the paternal uncle and paternal aunt according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Kafi: If he made a bequest to his relatives and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, it is divided between them in quarters. Similarly in his saying: to his close relatives, and to his uterine relatives, and to his lineages, and to his blood relatives. If he said: to his near relations or to his relative or to his relationship, the answer is what we mentioned, for here plurality is not considered according to Abu Hanifa, for the nearest then nearest enters the bequest, and one or more, without dispute. In al-Kafi: If he bequeathed to his near relations, plurality is not required for entitlement of all; even if he had a paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, all goes to the paternal uncle according to him. He said: In these matters, consideration is given to the relationship of the legatee at the time of the testator's death, not at the time of bequest. He said in al-Asl: If there is no mahram relative in these matters, the bequest is void according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Nawazil and al-Zahiriyya: If the relatives are too numerous to count, the scholars differed on the permissibility of the bequest; some said it is void. Muhammad ibn Salama said it is permissible and the fatwa is upon it because it is a kindness as it is a connection. If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to the testator... half and for them half; if he has a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt, they are equal; and to the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal; and to the heirs of his household, included in the bequest is everyone connected to him through his fathers up to the farthest father in Islam; the Muslim and disbeliever, male and female, mahram and non-mahram, near and distant are equal. A person's lineage is from his father's side, and everyone connected to him through his fathers up to the farthest father in Islam is from his household by lineage, so he enters under the bequest. The daughters' children do not enter under the bequest unless their husbands are from the testator's paternal cousins and tribe. The children of sisters do not enter, nor anyone from the mother's relatives of the testator. If he bequeaths to his kind, this is the same as if he bequeaths to his household, because a person is from the kind of his father's people; do you not see that Ibrahim, the son of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), was a Quraysh, and likewise the children of the caliphs are fit for the caliphate even if most of them were from slave women, and they are considered from the kind of their fathers' people. So his saying 'his kind' and his saying 'to his household' are the same. Everyone connected to him up to the farthest father in Islam enters under the bequest if he bequeaths to his family; this is the same as if he bequeaths to his household because they are used interchangeably; one says the family of Muhammad and the household of Muhammad, the family of Abbas and the household of Abbas. If he bequeaths one-third of his wealth to his family or to the household of so-and-so, the bequest is for the wife specifically, to the exclusion of others, by analogy, except that we applied istihsan and made the bequest for everyone who is his dependent, whose maintenance is obligatory upon him, and whom his house encompasses. His slaves do not enter under the bequest. If the family were in two towns or in two houses, they enter under the bequest due to the generality of the wording.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then it is for his two paternal uncles because they are closer, as in inheritance, and the plural form is used to mean the dual in bequest as we explained; so similarly here. This is according to Abu Hanifa; according to them, it is divided between them in quarters because they do not consider the closer relative. And it has preceded.) He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (If he has a paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, then for him half and for them half), meaning if he has (a paternal uncle) and two maternal uncles, then for the paternal uncle is half of what he bequeathed, and for the two maternal uncles the other half, because the wording is plural, so consideration of the meaning of plurality is necessary, which is to bring about the bequest as known; so the paternal uncle is joined with the maternal uncles to form a plural, so he takes half because he is closer, and they take half. Unlike if he bequeaths to his near relation, where all consideration of the bequest is for the paternal uncle since he is the closest. If he has only one relative, he gets half the bequest because we have stated that plurality must be considered, and the other half is returned to the heirs due to the lack of someone entitled to it, because the wording is plural and its minimum is two in bequest, so each gets half and the other half is returned to the heirs. He said: (If he has a paternal uncle and a paternal aunt, they are equal) because their relation is equal and the meaning of plurality is achieved by them, so they are entitled. Even if there are maternal uncles with them, they do not get anything because they are closer, and there is no need to join them because the quorum is complete with them. If the mahram relative is absent, the bequest is void because it is restricted to this condition, so it must be observed. All this according to Abu Hanifa. According to them, it is not void, nor are paternal uncles singled out for the bequest to the exclusion of maternal uncles, due to what is known of their school, and we have already explained it. He said: (And to the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal), meaning if he bequeaths to the children of so-and-so, male and female are equal.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explaining the rulings on bequests to relatives and other categories. It begins by establishing the principle that a bequest to 'aqarib' (relatives) goes to the nearest then the nearest, akin to inheritance. The author clarifies that the term 'aqarib' does not include parents or children, as they are not commonly called 'aqarib' in linguistic usage; rather, the Quranic verse (2:180) distinguishes between 'parents' and 'relatives' by conjunction, indicating mutual exclusivity. Grandparents and grandchildren are included in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), though a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf excludes them, directing the bequest to the farthest ancestor in Islam. The text then discusses the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the distribution when multiple relatives of different degrees exist. Abu Hanifa holds that the nearest relative takes the entire bequest, while the Sahibayn divide it equally among all relatives who fall under the term. The passage also explores the requirement of plurality: when the testator says 'to my relatives' (li-aqaribi), the plural form necessitates at least two recipients; if only one relative exists, half goes to that relative and half returns to the testator's heirs. Specific examples are given: with two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa gives the bequest to the paternal uncles (as they are closer), while the Sahibayn divide it into quarters among all four. With one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, Abu Hanifa gives half to the paternal uncle and half to the maternal uncles; the Sahibayn divide equally. The bequest is valid only if there is a mahram relative; otherwise, Abu Hanifa deems it void, while the Sahibayn uphold validity. The passage then addresses bequests to 'ahl baytihi' (his household), 'jinsihi' (his kind), and 'alihi' (his family). These terms are treated similarly, referring to all individuals connected to the testator through his paternal lineage up to the farthest Muslim ancestor, excluding children of daughters (unless their husbands are from the testator's paternal cousins) and relatives on the mother's side. A bequest to 'ahlihi' or 'ahl fulan' is, by analogy, limited to the wife, but istihsan expands it to all dependents whose maintenance is obligatory and who live with him. The passage concludes with the matn recapitulating the cases: the ruling for two paternal and two maternal uncles, one paternal and two maternal uncles, a paternal uncle and aunt, and children of so-and-so (where male and female are equal). Throughout, Abu Hanifa's positions are contrasted with those of the Sahibayn, with the text clearly stating the relied-upon view where applicable.

Key Terms
الأقرب فالأقرب (al-aqrab fa al-aqrab): The principle of 'the nearest then the nearest', analogous to inheritance distribution, applied by Abu Hanifa to bequests to relatives.
الصاحبان (al-Sahibayn): The two principal disciples of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. They often disagree with Abu Hanifa on subsidiary matters.
الفتوى (al-fatwa): The legal opinion that is adopted for practice; in this passage, the fatwa is upon the Sahibayn's view and Muhammad ibn Salama's view for numerous relatives.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the distribution under Abu Hanifa for a bequest to 'aqarib' when the testator leaves one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles?
A) The paternal uncle gets the entire bequest.
B) Each relative gets one third.
C) The paternal uncle gets half, the maternal uncles share half.
D) The bequest is void because no mahram relative.

Key Takeaway
The distribution of a bequest to relatives differs sharply between Abu Hanifa (nearest takes all, plural required) and the Sahibayn (equal division among all qualifying relatives), with the Sahibayn's view being the mufta bihi in later practice.

Validity of Bequest of Usufruct and Its Proof
States the ruling and proof for bequest of usufruct

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that bequest of usufruct (service, lodging, produce) is valid and explain the proof based on istihsan.

Core Idea
Bequest of benefits is valid by istihsan, just as benefits are transferable during life.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes the fundamental ruling that one can bequeath the service of a slave, lodging in a house, or produce of an asset, even though these are not physical assets. The author provides the rationale: benefits are validly transferable during life, and the same applies after death due to need, by analogy to physical assets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the statement of the ruling: 'وتصح الوصية بخدمة عبده وسكنى داره مدة معلومة وأبداً'. This declares the bequest of service and lodging valid, whether for a fixed term or perpetually.
The ruling covers both service and lodging; it is the core hukm.
2
Locate the proof
The proof follows immediately: 'لأن المنافع يصح تمليكها في حال الحياة ببدل أو بغير بدل وكذا بعد الممات للحاجة كما في حكم الأعيان'. Identify the key elements: ownership of benefits during life (by lease or gift) and extension after death due to need.
This is an istihsan argument, not a direct text.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the proof works: during life, benefits are validly owned with or without compensation. By istihsan, the same applies after death because of need, just as with physical assets (a'yān).
The analogy is to bequest of physical assets, which is universally accepted.
4
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may restrict bequest to physical assets, as usufruct is not considered inheritable property. Hanafi allows it based on istihsan and need.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
