Placing Objects in the Grave: The Pillow and the Shroud
Ruling on placing a pillow in the grave with dispute about stuffed items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on placing a pillow in the grave and distinguish between the permissibility of non-stuffed items and the dispute regarding stuffed items.

Core Idea
A pillow in the grave is like an addition to the shroud — but stuffing must be of the same material.

This lesson examines a specific funeral issue: is it permissible to place a pillow (mudarribah) beside the deceased in the grave? The primary answer is yes, as an extension of the shroud. However, a later objection raises a key distinction: stuffed items (mahshuww) are not of shroud material. We will trace the reasoning from the first response and the counter-argument based on the martyr's example.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and initial ruling
Read the opening question and response: Abu al-Nasr asks about placing something like a pillow in the grave. The answer is 'la ba'sa bihi' — no harm. This is the default Hanafi position.
The term 'mudarribah' refers to a pillow or cushion.
2
Understand the analogy to the shroud
The ruling states that the object is 'bimanzilati al-ziyadati fi al-kafan' — like an addition to the shroud. This means the object is treated as part of the burial wrapping, so it is permissible.
This analogy limits permissible objects to those that can be considered part of the shroud.
3
Examine the objection and its basis
In al-Khaniyyah, some scholars objected: if the object is stuffed (mahshuww), it does not remain under the body, and the stuffing is not of the same type (jins) as the shroud. This introduces a condition: the object must be of shroud material.
The key term 'mahshuww' means stuffed with cotton, feathers, etc.
4
Trace the martyr analogy
The objection cites Imam Muhammad's ruling about a martyr: weapons, fur, and stuffing are removed. If those items were considered part of the shroud, they would not have been ordered to be removed. This analogy supports the view that stuffed objects are not like the shroud.
The martyr case is a precedent (athar) from the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
The practical difference: non-stuffed items (e.g., a cloth pillow without filling) are permitted; stuffed items (e.g., a feather pillow) are subject to dispute. The mufta bihi is to avoid stuffed items as a precaution.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; both views are documented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سأل أبو النصر عن شيء يلقى في القبر بجنب الميت مثل المضربة ونحوها قال : لا بأس به وهو بمنزلة الزيادة في الكفن وفي الخانية : وبعضهم أنكر ذلك وقال: إذا كان محشواً لا تبقى تحته والمحشو ليس من جنس الكفن فقد ذكر محمد في حق الشهيد ينزع عنه السلاح والفرو والحشو، ولو كان من جنس الكفن لما أمر بنزعه
Abu al-Nasr asked about something that is placed in the grave next to the deceased, like a pillow and similar things. He said: There is no harm in it, and it is like an addition to the shroud. And in al-Khaniyyah: Some scholars objected to that and said: If it is stuffed, it does not remain underneath him, and the stuffing is not of the same type as the shroud. Muhammad mentioned regarding the martyr that weapons, fur, and stuffing are removed from him. If it were of the same type as the shroud, he would not have ordered its removal.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This is a ruling concerning placing objects like a pillow (mudarribah) beside the deceased in the grave. The initial response is that it is permissible and is like an addition to the shroud (kafan). However, in al-Khaniyyah, a counter-opinion is recorded: some scholars objected because if the object is stuffed (mahshuww), it will not remain under the body, and the stuffing is not of the same material as the shroud. They cite the precedent of Imam Muhammad regarding a martyr, from whom weapons, fur, and stuffing are removed; if such items were considered part of the shroud, they would not have been removed. This indicates that only items that are part of the shroud (like cloth) are allowed, not stuffed items like pillows.

Key Terms
المضربة (al-mudarribah): A pillow or cushion placed in the grave.
المحشو (al-mahshuww): Stuffed items, e.g., a pillow filled with cotton or feathers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objection mentioned in al-Khaniyyah, what is the basis for rejecting a stuffed pillow in the grave?
A) The pillow is too large for the grave.
B) The stuffing is not of the same type as the shroud.
C) The pillow will rot and cause harm.
D) The pillow is a sign of luxury forbidden in death.

Key Takeaway
Stuffed objects in the grave are not considered part of the shroud and thus their placement is subject to scholarly disagreement; the preferred view permits only items akin to the shroud.

Rulings on Executor Acceptance and Rejection
Ruling on executor acceptance and rejection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on an executor's acceptance and rejection and identify the effect of selling the estate.

Core Idea
An executor's explicit acceptance or rejection in the testator's presence is final; silence is not rejection.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins with a concise ruling on executor acceptance. Knowing when an executor's appointment becomes binding is essential for the proper administration of a will. This lesson clarifies that explicit verbal action in the testator's presence is required, and that selling the estate functions as acceptance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the testator appointing an executor. The ruling is that the executor's acceptance or rejection must be explicit (قبول/رد) and done in the presence of the testator. If done, it is effective; otherwise, it is not.
2
Understand the condition of presence
The key condition is that the acceptance or rejection occurs 'عنده' (in his presence). If the executor accepts or rejects elsewhere, the appointment may be pending.
This highlights the importance of direct communication in oral contract formation.
3
Analyze the implication of selling the estate
The matn states 'وبيع التركة كقبوله' – selling the estate by the executor is equivalent to acceptance. This action demonstrates intent to execute the role.
Even if the executor dies in a ruling sense (مات حكماً), the sale still counts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا/ باب الوصي وما يملكه
ولو أوصى إلى رجل فقبل عنده ورد عنده يرتد وإلا لا وبيع التركة كقبوله وإن مات حكماً
أوصى لمستأمن مثله ولو أعتق عبده عند الموت أو دبره جاز ذلك كله من غير تقييد بالثلث لما بينا، وكذا إذا أوصى له مسلم أو ذمي بوصية جاز لأنه ما دام في دار الإسلام كالذمي في المعاملات ولهذا تصح عقود التمليكات منه وتبرعاته في حال حياته فكذا عند مماته. وعن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف : وصية الذمي للحربي المستأمن لا تجوز لأنه في دراهم حتى يمكن من الرجوع إليها، والأول أظهر لأن الوصية تمليك مبتدأ ولهذا يجوز للذمي لأنهم التزموا أحكام الإسلام فيما يرجع إلى المعاملات. ولو أوصى لخلاف ملته جاز اعتباراً بالإرث لأن الكفر كاملة واحدة. ولو أوصى لحربي لا يجوز لأن الإرث ممتنع كتباين الدارين فكذا الوصية لأنها أخته، وعلى رواية الجامع الصغير ينبغي أن تجوز كالمسلم. ولو أوصى لمستأمن في دار الإسلام ينبغي أن يكون على الروايتين المذكورتين في المسلم والله أعلم.
Book of Bequests / Chapter of the Executor and What He Possesses. If he appoints a man as executor and [the executor] accepts in his presence and rejects in his presence, he has rejected; otherwise not. And selling the estate is like his acceptance, even if he dies in a ruling sense. He bequeathed to a musta'min like him. And if he frees his slave at death or makes him a mudabbar, all that is permissible without restriction to the third as we previously explained. Similarly, if a Muslim or a dhimmi bequeaths to him a bequest, it is permissible because as long as he is in Dar al-Islam, he is like a dhimmi in transactions, and therefore contracts of ownership from him and his donations during his life are valid, and likewise at his death. From Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: the bequest of a dhimmi to a harbi musta'min is not permissible because it is in dirhams until he can return to them. The first view is more apparent because the bequest is a new transfer of ownership, and therefore it is permissible for the dhimmi because they have accepted the rulings of Islam regarding transactions. And if he bequeaths to someone of a different religion, it is permissible by analogy to inheritance because disbelief is one single entity. And if he bequeaths to a harbi, it is not permissible because inheritance is prevented due to difference of dar, so too the bequest because it is its sister. According to the narration of al-Jami' al-Saghir, it should be permissible like a Muslim. And if he bequeaths to a musta'min in Dar al-Islam, it should be according to the two mentioned narrations about the Muslim, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins the chapter on the executor and his powers. The matn states that if a person appoints an executor and the executor accepts or rejects in the presence of the testator, his rejection is effective; otherwise, mere silence does not constitute acceptance. Selling the estate by the executor is equivalent to acceptance of the appointment. The commentary then discusses bequests to non-Muslims. A Muslim or dhimmi may bequeath to a musta'min (a non-Muslim given safe conduct) because in Dar al-Islam, he is treated like a dhimmi in financial transactions. However, there is a view from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf that a dhimmi's bequest to a harbi musta'min is invalid if the bequest is in dirhams, because the harbi musta'min cannot easily return to collect it. The preferred view (الأول أظهر) is that it is valid because a bequest is a new transfer of ownership (تمليك مبتدأ), and dhimmis have accepted Islamic transaction laws. Bequests to those of a different religion (non-Muslims) are permissible by analogy to inheritance, since disbelief is one class (الكفر كاملة واحدة). However, bequests to a harbi (an enemy non-Muslim in Dar al-Harb) are invalid because inheritance is impossible due to different dar, and the same applies to bequests. But according to a narration in al-Jami' al-Saghir, it may be permissible like to a Muslim. For a musta'min in Dar al-Islam, the ruling follows the two narrations about bequests to a Muslim.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): Executor appointed by the testator to carry out the will.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the effect if an executor, after being appointed, sells some of the testator's property without ever verbally accepting the appointment?
A) The sale is invalid because the executor never accepted.
B) The sale is considered acceptance of the executorship.
C) The appointment is revoked because the executor acted without authority.
D) The executor must still explicitly accept for the sale to be valid.

Key Takeaway
An executor's explicit acceptance or rejection in the testator's presence is binding; selling the estate indicates acceptance regardless of verbal statement.

Bequests to Musta'min, Dhimmi, and Harbi in Hanafi Fiqh
Explaining rulings on bequests to musta'min, dhimmi, and harbi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rulings on bequests to musta'min, dhimmi, and harbi, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a dhimmi's bequest to a harbi musta'min, and state the preferred position.

Core Idea
Bequests to non-Muslims in Dar al-Islam are generally valid, except to a harbi due to difference of dar.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the validity of bequests to non-Muslims. The Hanafi school considers that bequests to musta'min (temporary safe-conduct holders) and dhimmis (permanent non-Muslim subjects) are valid, as they are treated like Muslims in financial transactions. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about a dhimmi bequeathing to a harbi musta'min, and bequests to harbis (enemy non-Muslims) are generally invalid. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of non-Muslim beneficiaries
The passage mentions three types: musta'min (non-Muslim with safe conduct), dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of Islamic state), and harbi (non-Muslim from enemy territory). The ruling differs for each.
Musta'min is treated like dhimmi in transactions while in Dar al-Islam.
2
Understand the general rule for musta'min and dhimmi
Bequests to a musta'min are valid because during his stay in Dar al-Islam, he is like a dhimmi in transactions. Also, bequests to a dhimmi or someone of a different religion are valid by analogy to inheritance, as 'disbelief is one single entity' (الكفر كاملة واحدة).
This analogy (qiyas) is based on the idea that all non-Muslims share the same fundamental status regarding inheritance.
3
Note the dispute on a dhimmi's bequest to a harbi musta'min
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that such a bequest is invalid because the bequest is in dirhams and the harbi musta'min cannot easily return to collect it. The first view (الأول أظهر) is that it is valid because a bequest is a new transfer of ownership (تمليك مبتدأ) and dhimmis follow Islamic transaction laws.
The phrase 'الأول أظهر' indicates the preferred view in the text.
4
Distinguish harbi bequests
Bequests to a harbi are invalid due to difference of dar (تباين الدارين), which prevents inheritance. However, a narration from al-Jami' al-Saghir allows it like to a Muslim. For a musta'min in Dar al-Islam, the ruling follows the two narrations about bequests to a Muslim.
This shows that there is a weaker opinion permitting bequests to harbis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ذمي (dhimmi): A non-Muslim permanently residing in Dar al-Islam under a pact of protection.
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim from Dar al-Harb with whom Muslims are in a state of war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, is a bequest by a dhimmi to a harbi musta'min valid?
A) Yes, it is valid because a bequest is a new transfer of ownership.
B) No, it is invalid because the harbi cannot collect the money.
C) Valid only if the testator is Muslim.
D) Invalid because dhimmis cannot make bequests.

Key Takeaway
Bequests to musta'min and dhimmis are valid; bequests to harbis are invalid unless one accepts the narration from al-Jami' al-Saghir.

The Recommendation to Write a Will and Its Content
Explanation of the recommendation to write a will and its prescribed content.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith evidence for writing a will and identify the key elements that should be included in a will according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Writing a will is strongly recommended; a Muslim should not sleep without it.

This part of the commentary emphasizes the importance of preparing a will before death. The author cites a well-known hadith that a believer should have his will ready. He then provides a detailed template for the will's text, including statements of faith, acknowledgment of debts, and appointment of an executor. This lesson will help you understand the recommended content and the legal basis for writing a will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? The act of writing a will before death. The ruling is strongly recommended (sunnah mu'akkadah), though the hadith uses a prohibition form implying necessity.
The Hanafi school considers it sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, because the hadith is ahad and interpreted as a recommendation.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The hadith: 'It is not permissible for a man who believes in Allah and the Last Day to spend the night except with his will under his head.'
This hadith is widely reported but ahad; its thubut is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The phrase 'لا يحل' indicates prohibition of the negative (not having a will), which implies the obligation to have one. Hanafi usul treats such prohibitions as indicating wujub unless there is context for recommendation.
The Hanafi school uses the principle that al-nahy yufidu al-tahrim, but here the context (recommendation of the Prophet) leads to sunnah.
4
Identify the content of the will
What should be written in the will? The passage provides a detailed text that includes the testimony of faith, acknowledgment of debts, and appointment of an executor.
The sample text also includes declarations about Paradise, Hell, the Hour, and the testator's humility.
5
Note the ruling on witnessing
What condition is required for witnesses? The witness must know the content of the will; the hadith 'If you know like the sun, bear witness; otherwise leave it' requires certainty.
This applies to the gesture dispute in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فرغ من بيان أحكام الموصى له شرع في بيان أحكام الموصى إليه وهو الوصي، وقدم أحكام الموصى له لكثرتها وكثرة وقوعها فكانت الحاجة إلى معرفتها أمس. قال رحمه الله : (ولو أوصى إلى رجل فقبل عنده ورد عنده يرتد يعني قبل عند الموصي لأن الموصي ليس له ولاية إلزامه التصرف ولا عذر من جهته لأنه يمكنه أن إلى غيره. قال في الذخيرة : المراد بـ«عنده يعني بعلمه ورده بغير علمه سواء كان عنده أو في مجلس غيره. قال في المبسوط : مسألة مشتملة على فصول : فصل في حق الإيصاء وكيفيته، وفصل في قبوله ورده، وفصل فيمن يجوز إليه الإيصاء ومن لا يجوز، وفصل في عزله. الرجل إذا حضر الموت ينبغي أن يوصي ويكتب وصيته لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «لا يحل لرجل يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر يبيت إلا ووصيته تحت رأسه» ويكتب كتاب الوصية هذا ما أوصى فلان بن فلان فإنه يشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأن محمداً عبده ورسوله وأن الجنة حق والنار حق، وأن الساعة آتية لا ريب فيه وأن الله يبعث من في القبور وأن صلاتي ونسكي ومحياي ومماتي لله رب العالمين لا شريك له وبذلك أمرت وأنا أول المسلمين. أي في هذه الوصية لما روي عن النبي الله أنه قال من كان آخر كلمته شهادة إلا لا إله إلا الله وأني رسول الله وجبت الجنة ثم يكتب وأنا العبد المذنب الضعيف المفرط في طاعته المقصر في خدمته المفتقر إلى رحمته الراجي لفضله والهارب من عدله وترك من المال الصامت كذا، ومن الرقيق كذا، ومن الدور كذا، وعليه من الدين كذا إن كان عليه دين ويسمي الغريم واسم أبيه كيلا تجحد الورثة دينه فيبقى الميت تحت عهدته، ويكتب إن مت من مرضي هذا فأوصيت بأن يصرف مالي إلى وجوه الخيرات وأبواب البر تداركاً لما فرط في حياته وتزوداً وذخراً لآخرته، وأنه أوصى إلى فلان بن فلان ليقوم بقضاء ديونه وتنفيذ وصيته وتمهيد أسباب ورثته فعليه أن يتقي الله تقاته ولا يتقاعد في أموره في وصيته ولا يتقاصر عن إيفاء حقوقه واستيفائه، فإن تقاعد فإن الله تعالى حسب عليه ويشهد على ذلك. وإنما يصح الإشهاد إذا علم بما في الصك والشهادة على الوصية بدون العلم لا تجوز لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام للشاهد إذا علمت مثل الشمس فاشهدوا وإلا فدع ولو قال الشهود بعد ما قرؤوا الصك نشهد عليك فحرك رأسه بنعم ولم ينطق لم تجز شهادتهم، فإن اعتقل واحتبس لسانه روي عن أبي يوسف أنه تجوز وتعتبر إشارته وهو قول الشافعي له أن الإشارة تقوم مقام العبارة حاله عجزه عن النطق والعبادة قياساً على الأخرس لأن العجز عن النطق متى تحقق يستوي فيه العارض والأصلي فيما تتعلق صحته بالنطق كالعجز عن القراءة فإنه تجوز صلاة الأخرس بغير قراءة وتجوز صلاة من اعتقل لسانه بغير قراءة فكذا هذا ولنا أن الأشارة تدل على النطق والعبادة إنما تتصل إلى البدل حالة الياس عن النطق وهنا لم يقع اليأس عن النطق لأن اعتقال لسانه واحتباسه لا يدوم بل بعرض الزوال والانتقال في كل ساعة فلا تقوم الإشارة مقام العبارة، وأن الإشارة محتملة غير معلمة إلا أن في الأخرس تقدم منه إشارات مفهومة وآلة واضحة على مراداته الباطنة فزال الاحتمال عن إشاراته فقامت مقام نطقه وعبارته، وهنا لم يتقدم منه لم إشارات معلومة حتى يعلم بإشاراته مراداته فبقت إشارته محتملة غير مفهمة فلا تقوم مقام عبارته، فإما إذا طالت الغفلة أو الحبسة في لسانه ودام هل تعتبر أشارته؟ اختلف المشايخ فيه، قيل لا تعتبر اعتباراً للمعنى الأول وهو أنه لم يقع اليأس عن النطق فلا تقوم إشارته مقام عبارته، وقيل تعتبر وقد روي هذا أبو عمر والصغاني عن أبي حنيفة اعتباراً للمعنى الثاني لأنه لما طالت الغفلة صار له إشارة معهودة فتقوم مقام النطق كما في الأخرس وإضافة الوكالة إلى ما بعد الموت وصية لأن الإيصاء توكيل بعد الموت والوصاية قبل الموت وكالة. ولو أوصى إلى رجل في ماله كان وصياً فيه وفي ولده، وإذا أوصى إليه في أنواع وسكت عن نوع في نوع يكون وصياً في الأنواع كلها عندنا خلافاً للشافعي لأنه لو لم تعم وصايته تقع الحاجة إلى نصب وصي آخر فجعل من اختاره الميت وصياً ببعض أموره وصياً في كلها فالوصي.
He finished explaining the rulings of the legatee and began explaining the rulings of the person appointed as executor, i.e. the wasi. He presented the rulings of the legatee due to their abundance and frequency, so the need to know them was more pressing. He (the author) said: 'And if he appoints a man as executor and [the executor] accepts in his presence and rejects in his presence, he has rejected' meaning: he accepted in the presence of the testator because the testator does not have the authority to compel him to act, nor any excuse from his side because he can appoint someone else. In al-Dhakhira: 'in his presence' means with his knowledge, and rejection without his knowledge, whether in his presence or in another gathering. In al-Mabsut: This issue includes several sections: a section on the right of appointment and its manner, a section on its acceptance and rejection, a section on who may be appointed as executor and who may not, and a section on his dismissal. When death approaches, a man should make a will and write his will because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'It is not permissible for a man who believes in Allah and the Last Day to spend the night except with his will under his head.' And he writes the document of the will: 'This is what so-and-so son of so-and-so bequeaths: he bears witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, that Paradise is true and Hell is true, that the Hour is coming without doubt, and that Allah will resurrect those in the graves. And that my prayer, my sacrifice, my life and my death are for Allah, Lord of the worlds, no partner has He; with this I am commanded, and I am the first of the Muslims.' That is, in this will, because it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Whoever’s last words are the testimony that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah, Paradise becomes obligatory for him.' Then he writes: 'I am the sinful, weak servant, negligent in obedience, deficient in service, in need of His mercy, hoping for His bounty, fleeing from His justice, and I leave from the silent wealth such-and-such, from the slaves such-and-such, from the houses such-and-such, and I owe such-and-such debt if he has a debt, and he names the creditor and his father's name lest the heirs deny his debt and the deceased remains under its burden. He writes: 'If I die from this illness, I bequeath that my wealth be spent on good deeds and charitable causes as a recompense for what I neglected in life, provision and storage for my afterlife. And that he appointed so-and-so son of so-and-so to carry out the payment of his debts, execution of his will, and arranging the affairs of his heirs. So he must fear Allah with true piety, and not hold back in his affairs regarding his will, nor fall short in fulfilling his rights and collecting them. If he holds back, Allah Almighty will take account against him.' And he bears witness to that. And witnessing is only valid if he knows what is in the document; witnessing a will without knowledge is not permissible because of his statement (peace be upon him) to the witness: 'If you know like the sun, then bear witness; otherwise leave it.' And if the witnesses, after reading the document, say 'We testify against you' and he nods his head in affirmation but does not speak, their testimony is not valid. If his tongue becomes tied and seized, it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible and his gesture is considered, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i because the gesture stands in place of speech when he is unable to speak, by analogy to the mute. Because the inability to speak, once realized, the temporary and permanent are equal regarding matters whose validity depends on speech, like the inability to read: the prayer of a mute without recitation is valid, and the prayer of one whose tongue is tied without recitation is valid, so too this. Our argument: gesture indicates speech only as a substitute when despair of speech sets in, but here despair of speech has not occurred because the tying and seizing of his tongue does not last; rather it is subject to removal and change every hour, so the gesture does not stand in place of speech. And gesture is ambiguous and not clarifying, except that in the case of a mute, there are prior understood gestures and clear signs of his inner intentions, so ambiguity is removed from his gestures and they stand in place of his speech and expressions. Here, no known gestures preceded from him to indicate his intentions, so his gesture remains ambiguous and not understood, so it does not stand in place of his expression. If the loss of speech or the delay in his tongue continues and persists, is his gesture considered? The scholars differed: it is said it is not considered, considering the first meaning that despair of speech has not occurred, so his gesture does not stand in place of speech. And it is said it is considered, and this was narrated by Abu 'Umar and al-Sughani from Abu Hanifa, considering the second meaning that when the loss of speech persists, he develops familiar gestures that stand in place of speech like the mute. Adding the agency to after death is a will, because making a will is appointment after death, and executorship before death is agency. And if he appoints a man as executor over his wealth, he is an executor over it and over his children. And if he appoints him over types [of matters] and remains silent about one type, he is an executor over all types according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because if his executorship does not cover all, the need arises to appoint another executor, so the one chosen by the deceased as executor over some of his matters is made an executor over all of them. So the executor.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins with an introduction to the chapter on the executor. It explains the matn's ruling that acceptance or rejection of executorship is effective only if done in the presence of the testator. The commentary then emphasizes the recommendation to write a will before death, supported by the hadith ‘It is not permissible for a Muslim to spend the night without his will under his head.’ It then provides a recommended text for the will, including declarations of faith, acknowledgment of debts, and appointment of an executor. The passage then addresses a key legal issue: if a testator becomes unable to speak (aphasic) during the will, can his gestures (nodding, etc.) be accepted as valid expression? According to a narration from Abu Yusuf, gestures are valid, and this is also the view of al-Shafi'i, by analogy to a mute person. However, the preferred Hanafi position is that gestures are not equivalent to speech unless despair of recovery is certain, because temporary aphasia is not like permanent muteness. The gesture of a temporarily aphasic person is ambiguous and not reliable. But if the condition persists and he develops understood gestures, then according to a narration from Abu Hanifa, his gestures may be accepted. Finally, the passage discusses the scope of executorship: if a person is appointed executor over some matters, he is executor over all matters by default, unlike the Shafi'i school. This is to avoid the need for multiple executors.

Key Terms
إشارة (ishara): Gesture, such as nodding, used to communicate when unable to speak.
الأخرس (al-akhras): The mute person, who is permanently unable to speak.
اعتقال اللسان (i'tiqal al-lisan): Temporary inability to speak (aphasia), not permanent muteness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on writing a will?
A) Wajib (obligatory).
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah).
C) Mubah (permissible).
D) Haram (forbidden).

Key Takeaway
Writing a will is a strongly recommended act in the Hanafi school, and it should include the testimony of faith, acknowledgment of debts, and appointment of an executor.

10 min
Validity of Gestures for the Aphasic Testator
Explanation of the dispute on gestures of a testator who cannot speak.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on gestures of a temporarily aphasic testator and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
The gesture of a temporarily aphasic person is not a valid expression for a will unless his condition becomes permanent and he develops understood signs.

This lesson delves into a key dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the validity of gestures (ishara) for a testator who suddenly loses the ability to speak. The Hanafi school strictly distinguishes between temporary aphasia and permanent muteness, while al-Shafi'i and a narration from Abu Yusuf equate them. We will examine the proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What does the Hanafi school hold? The gestures of a temporarily aphasic testator are not valid for expressing the will because the inability is temporary and gestures are ambiguous; they only stand in place of speech when despair of recovery is certain and the gestures become familiar, like a permanent mute.
This is the relied-upon view, with a nuance that if the condition persists, another narration from Abu Hanifa accepts gestures.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Which school disagrees? Al-Shafi'i and a narration from Abu Yusuf hold that gestures are valid immediately, by analogy to a mute person.
The disagreement is based on the treatment of temporary vs. permanent inability.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
What is their evidence? They argue that the inability to speak makes the gesture a substitute for speech, similar to the mute; the temporary and permanent are equal in terms of the need for expression. They also cite the analogy to prayer: the mute's prayer without recitation is valid, and so is the prayer of one whose tongue is tied.
The analogy is qiyas: temporary aphasia is like permanent muteness in that both prevent speech.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
How does the Hanafi school rebut this? Despair of speech has not occurred in temporary aphasia; the gesture is ambiguous without prior established signs. The analogy to the mute fails because the mute has a habitual mode of communication, while the temporarily aphasic does not.
The Hanafi response distinguishes between 'ayaas (despair) and just inability.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? Under Hanafi, a will by gesture of a temporarily aphasic person is invalid unless his condition becomes permanent and he develops familiar gestures. Under Shafi'i, it would be valid immediately.
This affects how judges rule on wills made by nodding when the testator cannot speak.

He finished explaining the rulings of the legatee and began explaining the rulings of the person appointed as executor, i.e. the wasi. He presented the rulings of the legatee due to their abundance and frequency, so the need to know them was more pressing. He (the author) said: 'And if he appoints a man as executor and [the executor] accepts in his presence and rejects in his presence, he has rejected' meaning: he accepted in the presence of the testator because the testator does not have the authority to compel him to act, nor any excuse from his side because he can appoint someone else. In al-Dhakhira: 'in his presence' means with his knowledge, and rejection without his knowledge, whether in his presence or in another gathering. In al-Mabsut: This issue includes several sections: a section on the right of appointment and its manner, a section on its acceptance and rejection, a section on who may be appointed as executor and who may not, and a section on his dismissal. When death approaches, a man should make a will and write his will because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'It is not permissible for a man who believes in Allah and the Last Day to spend the night except with his will under his head.' And he writes the document of the will: 'This is what so-and-so son of so-and-so bequeaths: he bears witness that there is no god but Allah and that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger, that Paradise is true and Hell is true, that the Hour is coming without doubt, and that Allah will resurrect those in the graves. And that my prayer, my sacrifice, my life and my death are for Allah, Lord of the worlds, no partner has He; with this I am commanded, and I am the first of the Muslims.' That is, in this will, because it is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'Whoever’s last words are the testimony that there is no god but Allah and that I am the Messenger of Allah, Paradise becomes obligatory for him.' Then he writes: 'I am the sinful, weak servant, negligent in obedience, deficient in service, in need of His mercy, hoping for His bounty, fleeing from His justice, and I leave from the silent wealth such-and-such, from the slaves such-and-such, from the houses such-and-such, and I owe such-and-such debt if he has a debt, and he names the creditor and his father's name lest the heirs deny his debt and the deceased remains under its burden. He writes: 'If I die from this illness, I bequeath that my wealth be spent on good deeds and charitable causes as a recompense for what I neglected in life, provision and storage for my afterlife. And that he appointed so-and-so son of so-and-so to carry out the payment of his debts, execution of his will, and arranging the affairs of his heirs. So he must fear Allah with true piety, and not hold back in his affairs regarding his will, nor fall short in fulfilling his rights and collecting them. If he holds back, Allah Almighty will take account against him.' And he bears witness to that. And witnessing is only valid if he knows what is in the document; witnessing a will without knowledge is not permissible because of his statement (peace be upon him) to the witness: 'If you know like the sun, then bear witness; otherwise leave it.' And if the witnesses, after reading the document, say 'We testify against you' and he nods his head in affirmation but does not speak, their testimony is not valid. If his tongue becomes tied and seized, it is narrated from Abu Yusuf that it is permissible and his gesture is considered, and it is the saying of al-Shafi'i because the gesture stands in place of speech when he is unable to speak, by analogy to the mute. Because the inability to speak, once realized, the temporary and permanent are equal regarding matters whose validity depends on speech, like the inability to read: the prayer of a mute without recitation is valid, and the prayer of one whose tongue is tied without recitation is valid, so too this. Our argument: gesture indicates speech only as a substitute when despair of speech sets in, but here despair of speech has not occurred because the tying and seizing of his tongue does not last; rather it is subject to removal and change every hour, so the gesture does not stand in place of speech. And gesture is ambiguous and not clarifying, except that in the case of a mute, there are prior understood gestures and clear signs of his inner intentions, so ambiguity is removed from his gestures and they stand in place of his speech and expressions. Here, no known gestures preceded from him to indicate his intentions, so his gesture remains ambiguous and not understood, so it does not stand in place of his expression. If the loss of speech or the delay in his tongue continues and persists, is his gesture considered? The scholars differed: it is said it is not considered, considering the first meaning that despair of speech has not occurred, so his gesture does not stand in place of speech. And it is said it is considered, and this was narrated by Abu 'Umar and al-Sughani from Abu Hanifa, considering the second meaning that when the loss of speech persists, he develops familiar gestures that stand in place of speech like the mute. Adding the agency to after death is a will, because making a will is appointment after death, and executorship before death is agency. And if he appoints a man as executor over his wealth, he is an executor over it and over his children. And if he appoints him over types [of matters] and remains silent about one type, he is an executor over all types according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because if his executorship does not cover all, the need arises to appoint another executor, so the one chosen by the deceased as executor over some of his matters is made an executor over all of them. So the executor.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins with an introduction to the chapter on the executor. It explains the matn's ruling that acceptance or rejection of executorship is effective only if done in the presence of the testator. The commentary then emphasizes the recommendation to write a will before death, supported by the hadith ‘It is not permissible for a Muslim to spend the night without his will under his head.’ It then provides a recommended text for the will, including declarations of faith, acknowledgment of debts, and appointment of an executor. The passage then addresses a key legal issue: if a testator becomes unable to speak (aphasic) during the will, can his gestures (nodding, etc.) be accepted as valid expression? According to a narration from Abu Yusuf, gestures are valid, and this is also the view of al-Shafi'i, by analogy to a mute person. However, the preferred Hanafi position is that gestures are not equivalent to speech unless despair of recovery is certain, because temporary aphasia is not like permanent muteness. The gesture of a temporarily aphasic person is ambiguous and not reliable. But if the condition persists and he develops understood gestures, then according to a narration from Abu Hanifa, his gestures may be accepted. Finally, the passage discusses the scope of executorship: if a person is appointed executor over some matters, he is executor over all matters by default, unlike the Shafi'i school. This is to avoid the need for multiple executors.

Key Terms
إشارة (ishara): Gesture, such as nodding, used to communicate when unable to speak.
الأخرس (al-akhras): The mute person, who is permanently unable to speak.
اعتقال اللسان (i'tiqal al-lisan): Temporary inability to speak (aphasia), not permanent muteness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does the gesture of a testator with a tied tongue (aphasic) become valid?
A) Immediately when he becomes unable to speak.
B) If the condition persists and he develops familiar, understood gestures.
C) Never, only written will is valid.
D) Only if witnessed by two qualified witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not accept gestures from a temporarily aphasic testator unless his condition becomes permanent and he develops understood signs, ensuring certainty in legal transactions.

The Core Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Joint vs Independent Action of Executors
Intra-Hanafi dispute with ta'lil and subsidiary cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi default ruling on multiple executors and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad versus Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
When multiple executors are appointed, joint action is required; independent action is void (suspended) per Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

This lesson examines a well-known internal Hanafi dispute regarding the authority of executors (awṣiyā). The central question: if a testator appoints two executors, may one act independently, or must they act jointly? The default position, held by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybānī, is that no single executor may act alone; any such act is void (bāṭil) or suspended (mawqūf) pending the other's ratification. Abu Yūsuf disagrees, arguing that each executor has full authority like a guardian (walī). We will unpack the proofs and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is the independent transaction of one executor when two (or more) are appointed. The default ruling according to the text: it is invalid (bāṭil) but interpreted as suspended (mawqūf) pending the other executor's approval.
Note the nuance: 'bāṭil' here does not mean absolutely void, but void unless the other executor ratifies.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: the act is void/suspended. Abu Yusuf: each executor may act independently. Identify the advocates of each view.
The third major Hanafi figure, Muhammad al-Shaybānī, agrees with Abu Hanifa, making the majority position.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof (dalil)
Abu Yusuf analogizes executorship to guardianship (wilāyah), which is indivisible; thus each executor possesses full authority, just as two brothers each have independent guardianship in marriage.
His reasoning: the testator's appointment of each shows trust in each individually.
4
Analyze the majority's response
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad counter that guardianship in marriage is based on kinship (qarābah), an indivisible cause, whereas executorship is based on appointment (ikhtiyār). The testator's appointment of two indicates a need for joint deliberation; each is like 'half a cause' (sharṭ al-illah) and cannot alone produce the effect.
They also distinguish executorship from agency (wakālah) because the principal is alive in agency, so separate appointments imply independent authority.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical difference: if an executor acts alone, under the majority the act is suspended; under Abu Yusuf it is valid. The relied-upon position (muftā bihi) is the majority view: joint action is required unless the testator explicitly permits independence.
This affects the heirs' ability to challenge sole actions.

Source Text

الوصي
:

قال الفقيه أبو الليث وبعضهم قالوا كلاهما وصيان في الوجهين جميعاً. وقال بعضهم : الأول هو الوصي وبه قال نصير. وقال أبو نصر : إن قال اعمل فيه برأي فلان فهو خاصة، وإن قال لا تعمل إلا برأي فلان فهما وصيان وهو أشبه بقول أصحابنا فإنهم قالوا فيمن وكل آخر ببيع عبده وقال بالشهود فباعه الوكيل بغير شهود جاز، وكذلك لو قال بعه بمحضر فلان فباعه بغير محضر فلان يجوز ولو قال لا تبع إلا بالشهود أو قال لا تبع إلا بمحضر من فلان فباع بغير شهود أو بغير محضر فلان لا يجوز، وعلى هذا إذا قال الموصي بعلم فلان أو قال إلا بعلم فلان وإذا أوصى الرجل إلى رجلين وقال لهما ضعا ثلث مالي حيث شئتما أو قال أعطياه ممن شئتما ثم اختلفا في ذلك فقال أحدهما أعطيه فلاناً وقال الآخر أعطيه فلاناً آخر لم يكن لواحد منهما ذلك عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف. وفي الخانية : رجل أوصى بنصيب بعض ولده إلى رجل وبنصيب البعض إلى رجل آخر فهما يشتركان في الكل، ولو أوصى إلى رجل بدين وإلى آخريان يعتق عبده أو ينفذ وصيته فهما وصيان في كل شيء في قول أبي حنيفة. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد كل واحد منهما وصي على ما له لا يدخل الآخر معه، وكذا لو أوصى بميراثه في بلد كذا إلى رجل وبميراثه في بلد كذا إلى رجل وبميراثه في بلد أخرى إلى آخر. وقال الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل : إذا جعل الرجل رجلاً وصياً على ابنه وجعل رجلاً آخر وصياً على ابنه أو جعل أحدهما وصياً في ماله الحاضر وجعل الآخر وصياً في ماله الحاضر وجعل الآخر وصياً في ماله الغائب، فإن كان شرط أن لا يكون كل واحد منهما وصياً فيما أوصى إلى الآخر يكون الأمر على ما شرط عند الكل، وإن لم يكن شرط ذلك فحينئذ تكون المسألة على الاختلاف، والفتوى على قول أبي حنيفة وفي الوصيتين من جهة الأبوين ومعهم وصي الأم قال محمد في
سمي
Chapter of Wills / Section on the Executor and His Powers / Invalidity of an act of one of two executors except in preparation, purchasing the shroud, and needs of minors. He (the author) said: (And the act of one of the two executors is void) i.e., if a person appoints two executors, it is not permissible for either of them to act regarding the property of the deceased; if he acts, it is void. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: Each of them may act independently. Then it is said: The dispute is when he appointed each of them with a separate contract. As for when he appointed them together, or appointed them with separate contracts but the issue is when there are two contracts; as for one contract, neither acts alone by consensus. Thus mentioned by al-Kayyasani. And it is said: The dispute applies to both cases, mentioned by Abu Bakr al-Iskaff. And it is said in al-Mabsut: That is more correct. It is clear that by 'invalidity' is meant suspension pending the other's permission or rejection, unlike two agents if he appointed them separately, where each acts alone by consensus. The difference is that joining the second in appointment is evidence of the first's inability to act alone, because joining the second aims at partnership with the first, and he has the right to revoke the first's appointment, so he can include the second. And a person may appoint someone thinking he can accomplish his purpose alone, then realizes his inability, so he joins another, making it like appointing them together. This is not the case in agency, because the principal is alive; if the agent was incapable, he would act himself, since he can. And when he appointed an agent, it is known that his intention is that each acts independently. Also, the obligation of executorship arises at death, so it is established for both together, unlike successive agency. Since it is established that the dispute applies to both cases, Abu Yusuf says: Executorships are a form of guardianship (wilayah), which is a legal attribute that cannot be divided; so each is established fully, like the guardianship of marriage for two brothers. This is because executorship is a deputyship, and deputyship is only realized when it transfers to him similarly. The testator's choice of them indicates that each has exclusive affection towards him. And they (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say: Guardianship arises at death, so its characteristic is considered, which is jointness, because it is a beneficial condition: the opinion of one is not like that of two, and the testator did not approve of less than two. So each one in this regard is like half of the cause, and it does not establish a ruling, so it is void. This is unlike the two brothers in marriage because the cause there is kinship, and it is fully established in each. Also, marriage is a right that she has against the guardian; if she demands that he marry her to a suitable suitor, it becomes obligatory. Here, the right to act is for the executor, and for this reason he remains free to choose whether to act. So in the case of two guardians (in marriage), it is incumbent upon each to act for the other; but in the case of two executors, each one claims a right for himself, so it is invalid. The analogy is: the first is like payment of a debt on them both; the second is like collection of a debt for them both, where the first is allowed but not the second. Exceptions are areas of necessity, which are always excluded, as mentioned in the text and its parallels. In al-Tatar Khaniyya: A man appointed two executors; one died and appointed the other as his executor; this is valid, and the other can act. It is also narrated that it is not valid, but the first is correct. In Fatawa Abi Layth: If he appointed two executors, one accepted and the other remained silent, then the one who accepted said to the silent one after the testator's death: 'Buy this for the deceased,' and he said 'Yes,' that constitutes acceptance of executorship... [and so on]
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discusses the ruling on multiple executors (al-wasiyyan). The core issue is whether one executor can act independently when two are appointed, or if they must act jointly. The author begins by stating the default ruling: if a person appoints two executors, neither may act alone; any such action is void (bāṭil). This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybānī (the two major disciples of Abu Hanifa). Abu Yūsuf disagrees, holding that each executor may act independently. The text then explores the scope of the dispute: does it apply only when each executor is appointed by a separate contract, or also when they are appointed together? Some scholars distinguish, but the preferred view (al-aṣaḥḥ) is that the dispute applies to both scenarios. Importantly, 'void' here means the action is suspended (mawqūf) pending the other executor's ratification or rejection, unlike the case of two agents (wakīlān) who, if appointed separately, can each act alone by consensus. The reason for the difference is that appointing a second executor indicates the first's inability to manage alone, and the testator's intention is joint action. In agency, the principal is alive and could have acted himself, so separate appointment implies trust in each to act independently. Abu Yūsuf analogizes executorship to guardianship (wilāya), which is indivisible; each executor should have full authority, like two brothers who both have guardianship in marriage. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad counter that guardianship in marriage is based on kinship, which is inherent, whereas executorship is based on the testator's choice, and he chose both, so joint action is required. The text then presents numerous subsidiary rulings: what happens if one executor dies and appoints the other as his executor, whether a silent executor's later action constitutes acceptance, how to handle differences of opinion about distribution, and cases where executors are appointed for different assets or children. The relied-upon position (al-fatwā) is generally that of Abu Hanifa, requiring joint action unless the testator explicitly allows independent action.

Key Terms
وصي (waṣī): An executor appointed by a testator to manage the estate and execute the will.
وصيان (waṣiyyān): Two executors appointed jointly or separately; the default rule is that they must act together unless the testator stipulates otherwise.
ولاية (wilāyah): Guardianship or authority; in this context, Abu Yusuf argues that executorship partakes of wilāyah, which is indivisible.
وكالة (wakālah): Agency; a contract where one authorizes another to act on his behalf while alive.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the default ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad when a person appoints two executors without specifying that they may act independently?
A) Each executor may act independently.
B) Neither executor may act alone; any sole action is void or suspended.
C) Only the first appointed executor may act alone.
D) The executors must appoint a third to decide.

Key Takeaway
The default Hanafi rule requires joint action when multiple executors are appointed; a single executor's act is void unless ratified by the others or explicitly permitted by the testator.

Rulings on the Insane Person (Ma'tuh) - Time Limit for Valid Transactions
Ruling on validity of ma'tuh's transactions after time limit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the time limit for when a ma'tuh's transactions become valid after the onset of insanity and explain the intra-Hanafi difference on that duration.

Core Idea
A ma'tuh's transactions are invalid for one year from onset, then valid, like a majnun.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a specific ruling regarding the insane person (ma'tuh). While the general rule equates ma'tuh with majnun, there is a nuance about the duration of prohibition on transactions. The text presents the dominant view of one year, with a reported variation from Imam Muhammad of one month. Understanding this ruling is important because it affects the validity of financial dealings during an illness that impairs intellect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage discusses transactions (تصرفات) by a ma'tuh (mentally incapacitated person). The ruling states that these are not valid until a year passes from the day he became ma'tuh.
Ma'tuh is distinguished from a fully insane person (majnun) in terminology but shares the same legal rulings.
2
Note the sources and gaps
The author (likely the commentator of al-Bahr al-Raiq) says he does not recall any explicit statement from Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf on this specific point. This indicates the ruling is derived from general principles.
This is a case of nawadir — a transmission from Muhammad al-Shaybani that is not from the well-known six books.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Ibn Sama'a reports that Imam Muhammad set the period as one month instead of one year. This is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
The mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) is the one-year period, as it aligns with the general rule for junun.
4
Apply the principle of equality between ma'tuh and majnun
The passage concludes that any known ruling for junun applies equally to ma'tuh. Thus, the time limit for the interdiction of a ma'tuh is the same as for a majnun: one year.
This principle simplifies the legal treatment: you can look up rulings for insanity and apply them here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعتوه والتصرف عليه لا يصح حتى تمضي عليه سنة من يوم صار معتوهاً قال : ولا أحفظ فيه عن أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف شيئاً. قال ابن سماعة قال محمد: وقت في ذلك شهراً ثم بعد رجوعه من الذي قدره بسنة وكل جواب عرفته في الجنون فهو الجواب في المعتوه لأنهما يستويان في الأحكام.
The insane person (ma'tuh) and transactions upon him are not valid until a year passes from the day he became insane. He said: I do not recall anything about this from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Ibn Sama'a said: Muhammad allotted a month for that, then after his return, [the validity] is from what he estimated with a year. And every answer I know regarding insanity (junun) is the answer for the insane (ma'tuh), because they are equal in rulings.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage addresses the validity of transactions by an insane person (ma'tuh). The base ruling is that such transactions are invalid for one full year from the onset of insanity. The text notes that no explicit statement from Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf is preserved on this specific point. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani is reported to have set the period at one month instead. The important principle stated is that the rulings for insanity (junun) apply equally to being mentally incapacitated (ma'tuh), so all legal rules for the insane apply here as well.

Key Terms
معتوه (ma'tuh): A person who is mentally incapacitated, not fully insane but lacking intellect.
جنون (junun): Insanity, a legal cause for interdiction of property transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For how long are a ma'tuh's transactions considered invalid from the onset of the condition according to the mufta bihi?
A) One month
B) One year
C) Until a judge declares restoration of sanity
D) Indefinitely

Key Takeaway
A ma'tuh's transactions are invalid for one year from onset, then valid, following the same rule as for majnun.

Usurper of Orphan's Property Must Pay Rent
Ruling on usurper of minor's property and exception for orphan's benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a usurper of an orphan's property and identify the exceptional case where reduction is preferred.

Core Idea
Usurping an orphan's property obligates equivalent rent, but benefit to the orphan may permit a reduction instead.

This passage addresses a specific case of ghasb (usurpation) involving the property of a minor. While the general rule is compensation through equivalent rent, the school considers the orphan's welfare, allowing an exception. Let us examine the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is usurping (ghasb) the property of a minor or orphan. The ruling is that the usurper must pay the equivalent rent (ajr al-mithl) for the period of use.
This is a wajib (obligatory) compensation.
2
Note the exception
Some mashayikh narrated that if the reduction in value (naqsan) is better for the orphan, then the reduction is preferred over full equivalent rent.
The exception is based on the orphan's best interest.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The Hanafi school prioritizes the welfare of the orphan, allowing flexibility in compensation if it benefits the orphan.
This is consistent with the guardian's duty to act in the orphan's best interest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال بعض الصغير . قال القاضي ركن الإسلام علي السغدي لو غصب إنسان دار صبي الناس يجب عليه أجره المثل فما ظنك في هذا؟ ومن المشايخ من روي وجوب أجر المثل إلا إذا كان النقصان خيراً للصغير فحينئذ يحب النقصان.
Some of the young [scholars] said. Qadi Rukn al-Islam Ali al-Sughdi said: If a person usurps the house of an orphan, he must pay its equivalent rent. So what do you think about this? And from the mashayikh, some narrated the obligation of the equivalent rent unless the reduction is better for the orphan, then the reduction is preferred.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Qadi Rukn al-Islam Ali al-Sughdi regarding a person who usurps the property of a minor (sabi) or orphan (yatim). The ruling is that the usurper must pay the equivalent rent (ajr al-mithl) for the period of usurpation. This is analogous to the general principle that one who wrongfully uses another's property must compensate. However, some scholars (mashayikh) have narrated an exception: if the reduction in value (naqsan) is actually beneficial for the orphan (e.g., if the property would have deteriorated anyway), then the reduction is preferred over rent. This shows a consideration of the orphan's best interest. The phrase 'fama zannuka fi hadha' is a rhetorical question emphasizing the obviousness of the ruling.

Key Terms
غصب (ghasb): Usurpation, taking another's property wrongfully without right.
أجر المثل (ajr al-mithl): The equivalent rent or compensation for use of property, determined by market value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a person who usurps a minor's property?
A) He must return the property only.
B) He must pay the equivalent rent.
C) He must pay double the value.
D) He is exempt if the property is returned.

Key Takeaway
Usurping an orphan's property obligates equivalent rent, but the reduction may be taken if it is more beneficial for the orphan.

Executor's Authority: Sale and Division of Estate
Ruling with proof on executor's sale and division authority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the limits of an executor's authority to sell estate property, explain why division is treated as a sale, and identify conditions for valid transactions.

Core Idea
An executor is an amin with limited sale authority: movables yes, immovables no; division is like a sale.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the boundaries of an executor's power over the estate. Understanding these boundaries is crucial because an executor who oversteps invalidates transactions. The key distinction is between movable and immovable property, and the legal treatment of division as a sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the executor's legal status
Recognize that the executor is an amin (trustee) over the estate, meaning he is not liable for accidental loss. This status underlies his authority and liability.
Amin status is default; liability arises only from negligence.
2
Distinguish movables vs immovables for sale
The executor may sell movables of minors and adults for preservation. He cannot sell immovable property (aqar) because it is self-preserving.
Selling immovables is void (not merely invalid) unless necessity is proven.
3
Understand division (qisma) as a sale
Division among heirs is treated as a sale in meaning (fi ma'na al-bay'), so the same rules apply: the executor can divide movables, and he is not liable if property perishes during division.
This affects liability and permissibility of division for absent heirs.
4
Recognize special rules for minors
The executor can sell movables of minors for their benefit, but cannot sell one minor's share to another without a clear benefit; division between two minors is not permissible because it harms one.
A hila (legal stratagem) is provided to achieve division through an intermediary sale.
5
Apply the rule to mixed heirs (minors and absent adults)
If heirs include minors and absent adults, the executor may divide movables (treating absent adults like minors) but not immovables. If adults are present, division among adults is permissible.
This is based on the principle that absent adults are deemed like minors for practical necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيع يضمن لأنه أمين فيه وله ولاية الحفظ في التركة كما إذا هلك بعض التركة قبل القسمة فيكون له ثلث الباقي لأن الموصى له شريك الورثة فيتوى ما توى ما المال المشترك على الشركة ويبقى ما بقي من على الشركة وله البيع في مال الصغار والقسمة في معنى البيع وله ولاية الحفظ في مال الكبار فجاز له بيعه للحفظ إلا العقار فإنه محفوظ بنفسه فلا يجوز له بيعه، وقسمته على الورثة الكبار حال غيبتهم في معنى البيع فلا يضمن إذا هلك في يده. وفي المبسوط : وقسمة الوصي إما أن تكون مع الموصى له أو فيما بين الورثة أما قسمته مع الموصى له جائزة مع الصغار وفي المنقول وقبض نصيبهم، وأما في العقار لا تجوز على الكبير لأن القسمة معنى وله ولاية بيع المنقول على الكبار دون بيع العقار ؛ هكذا ذكره في المبسوط. وذكر في اختلاف زفر ويعقوب أن القسمة في العقار لا تجوز عند أبي حنيفة وزفر، وعند أبي يوسف ومحمد تجوز قسمة الوصي على الموصى له الغائب مع الورثة. وذكر في اختلاف زفر ويعقوب أن عند أبي يوسف تجوز لأن الميت أقام الوصي مقام نفسه وأثبت الولاية له فيما يحتاج إليه عند عجزه بنفسه وهو يحتاج في تنفيذ وصاياه إلى إيصال التركة إلى الورثة لأنه يثاب بوصول التركة إلى الورثة كما يثاب بوصول الوصية إلى الموصى له فيجب أن يملك ذلك نظراً للموصى. وعلى قياس قوله يجب أن يملك القسمة على الكبار الحضور وقضاء الدين من الحاجة الفاضلة فيمكن تأخيرها إذا امتنعوا عن القسمة حتى يحضر الغائب بخلاف الحاجة الضرورية لا يمكن تأخيرها لأن في التأخير توهم الضياع وفي الضياع ضرر على الميت فلا يجوز تأخيرها وفي تأخير الحاجة الفاضلة وإن كانت توهم الضياع وفي الضياع ضرر على الميت إلا أنه لا ضرر فيه على الميت فيجوز تأخيرها، وفي كل موضع لا تحل القسمة إذا ضاع أحد النصيبين يضيع على الشركة وما يبقى يبقى على الشركة وقسمة الوصي الميراث بين الصغار لا يجوز لأن القسمة بمعنى البيع ولا يجوز شراء الوصي مال أحد الصغيرين للصغير الآخر لأن بيعه مقيد بشرط أن يكون فيه منفعة ظاهرة للصغير فإن كان لأحدهما فيه منفعة ظاهرة يكون للآخر فيه مضرة ظاهرة فلم يجز البيع فلم تجز القسمة . . وعند محمد لا يلي من الجانبين بكل حال والحيلة في جواز هذه القسمة أن حصة أحد الصغيرين مشاعاً، يبيع وإن كانوا ثلاثة باع حصة أحد الصغار من آخر ثم يقاسم مع المشتري ثم حصة أحد الصغيرين كي يمتاز حق أحدهما عن الآخر. وإن كانوا الورثة صغاراً وكباراً والكبار غيب لا تجوز قسمته في العقار لأنه لا يلي بيعه على الكبار فكذلك قسمته، وفي العروض له ولاية القسمة كما يلي بيعها لأن الكبار الغيب التحقوا بالصغار في هذه الحالة فصار كأن الكل صغار. ولو كان الكل صغاراً تجوز قسمته فكذا هذا، وإن كان الكبار حضوراً جاز قسمته الكبار لأن هذه قسمة جرت بين اثنين والقسمة بين الصغار جرت من الواحد عن الصغار مع العقد لأنه لا يلي القسمة من الجانبين فلم تجز القسمة في حق الصغار جملة فالقسمة في حق الكبار
He is liable because he is a trustee over it, and he has the authority of preservation over the estate, as when part of the estate perishes before division, then he gets one-third of the remainder because the legatee is a partner with the heirs; what perishes does so from the joint property, and what remains remains on joint ownership. He has the right to sell the property of minors, and division is in the meaning of sale. He has the authority of preservation over the property of adults, so it is permissible for him to sell it for preservation, except immovable property because it is preserved by itself, so it is not permissible for him to sell it. His division among the adult heirs in their absence is in the meaning of sale, so he is not liable if it perishes in his hand. In al-Mabsut: The executor's division is either with the legatee or among the heirs. As for his division with the legatee, it is permissible with minors in movables and taking their shares. As for immovable property, it is not permissible over the adult because division is a meaning, and he has authority to sell movables to adults but not to sell immovable property. Thus it is mentioned in al-Mabsut. And it is mentioned in Ikhtilaf Zufar wa Ya'qub that division of immovable property is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Zufar, while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the executor's division among the absent legatee with the heirs is permissible. And it is mentioned in Ikhtilaf Zufar wa Ya'qub that according to Abu Yusuf it is permissible because the deceased appointed the executor in his place and established authority for him in what he needs due to his own incapacity, and he needs for the execution of his bequests to deliver the estate to the heirs, for he receives reward by the delivery of the estate to the heirs just as he receives reward by the delivery of the bequest to the legatee, so he must have that right out of consideration for the testator. By analogy with his statement, he must have the right to divide among the present adults and to pay debts from the surplus need; it can be delayed if they refuse the division until the absent person arrives, unlike a necessary need which cannot be delayed because in delay there is fear of loss, and in loss there is harm to the deceased, so it cannot be delayed. In delaying a non-essential need, even if there is fear of loss and in loss there is harm to the deceased, yet there is no harm to the deceased in it, so it can be delayed. In every situation where division is not valid, if one of the two shares is lost, it is lost from the joint ownership, and what remains remains on joint ownership. The executor's division of inheritance among minors is not permissible because division is in the meaning of sale, and it is not permissible for the executor to buy the property of one minor for another minor because his sale is restricted to the condition that there be an obvious benefit for the minor. If there is an obvious benefit for one, there is obvious harm for the other, so the sale is not permissible, and thus the division is not permissible. According to Muhammad, he does not act on behalf of both sides in any case. The legal stratagem to make this division permissible is that the share of one of the two minors is sold as an undivided share; if there are three, he sells the share of one minor to another, then divides with the buyer, then the share of one of the two minors so that the right of one is distinguished from the other. If the heirs are minors and adults, and the adults are absent, his division of immovable property is not permissible because he cannot sell it to adults, and likewise his division. In the case of movables, he has authority to divide just as he has authority to sell them, because absent adults are considered like minors in this situation, so it is as if all are minors. If all were minors, his division would be permissible, so likewise this. If the adults are present, his division among the adults is permissible because this division occurs between two parties, and division among minors occurs from one party on behalf of the minors with the contract because he does not act on behalf of both sides, so the division is not permissible with respect to minors at all; the division with respect to adults remains.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, explaining the scope of an executor's (wasi) authority over the estate. The author begins by stating a key principle: the executor is a trustee (amin) over the estate, meaning he is not liable for loss unless he is negligent. However, he has the authority to preserve the estate. If some property perishes before division, the legatee (who is entitled to one-third of the estate) is considered a partner with the heirs; loss is shared proportionally. The executor's authority includes selling the movable property of minors for their benefit, and dividing the estate among heirs. Division is treated analogically as a sale (qisma fi ma'na al-bay'), so the same rules apply regarding liability and permissibility. The executor is not liable for loss during division. He can also sell the movable property of adult heirs for preservation, but cannot sell immovable property (aqar) because it is inherently self-preserving. The text then cites al-Mabsut, distinguishing division with the legatee (musa lahu) versus division among heirs. Division with the legatee is permissible for minors in movables. For adults, immovable property division is not permissible due to lack of authority. An intra-Hanafi dispute is recorded: Abu Hanifa and Zufar hold that executor cannot divide immovable property for absent adults, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it, reasoning that the testator delegated authority to the executor for necessary tasks, and delivering the estate to heirs is a rewardable act like delivering the bequest. The latter view is supported by analogy: just as the executor can pay debts from surplus, he can divide immovable property. However, if the need is not urgent, it can be delayed to avoid harm to the deceased. The text then discusses division among minors: it is not permissible for the executor to divide between two minors because it is like a sale between them, which would harm one. Muhammad holds he cannot represent both sides. A legal stratagem (hila) is provided: sell the share of one minor as an undivided share to an outsider, then divide with the buyer, then sell the share to the other minor to separate rights. When heirs include both minors and absent adults, division of movables is allowed because absent adults are treated like minors; present adults, the division is permissible. The passage ends by affirming that division among present adults is valid because it is between two parties, but division among minors is invalid because the executor acts for both sides, which is not allowed.

Key Terms
أمين (amin): Trustee who is not liable for loss unless negligent; executor is amin over estate.
قسمة (qisma): Division of jointly owned property among co-owners; here, executor's division is treated as a sale in terms of legal effect.
ولاية (wilaya): Legal authority to act on behalf of another; executor has wilayat al-hifz (authority of preservation) and wilayat al-bay' (authority to sell) within limits.
عقار (aqar): Immovable property (land, buildings); considered self-preserving, executor cannot sell it except in necessity.
منقول (manqul): Movable property (goods, animals, etc.); executor has authority to sell for preservation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why can an executor not sell the immovable property (aqar) of adult heirs for preservation?
A) Because the executor lacks authority over adults' property
B) Because immovable property is preserved by itself and does not require sale
C) Because the heirs can sell it themselves
D) Because the executor is only a trustee over movables

Key Takeaway
An executor's authority to sell is limited to movables for preservation; division is like a sale, and immovables cannot be sold or divided without necessity.

Division by Two Executors and Legatee's Recourse
Ruling on division by two executors among heirs and the case of legatee's share perishing after division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why division by two executors is invalid and state the legatee's recourse when his share perishes after an invalid division.

Core Idea
Two executors are one agent; division requires two parties, so their division is void—the legatee can recover from whoever wrongfully possessed his share.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, we examine two interconnected rulings on executorship. First, why can't two executors validly divide the estate among themselves? Second, if they do and the legatee's share is lost, who bears the loss? The key insight is that executors represent the deceased as a single entity, so they cannot contract with themselves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: two executors dividing the estate among the heirs and themselves. Identify the hukm: the division is invalid (fasid).
The text says 'فالقسمة فاسدة'.
2
Understand the legal reason
The illa is that division requires two distinct parties, but both executors represent the same deceased, so they are like one person. Therefore, they cannot be parties to a division with each other.
Analogy: a trustee cannot sell trust property to himself.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
According to Abu Yusuf, one executor can act alone, but when both act together, each is a partner of the other, making the division invalid. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that both are like one person, so neither can divide alone.
This difference appears in the text: 'عندهما' vs 'عند أبي يوسف'.
4
Apply to the legatee's loss scenario
If the executor divided and gave the legatee's share to the heirs, and that share perished, the legatee is considered a partner of the heirs. Thus, he can take one-third of what remains in the hands of the heirs.
The legatee's right remains because the division was invalid with respect to his share.
5
Identify the legatee's options for recourse
The legatee can choose to hold either the executor or the heirs liable for the value of his share. The executor is liable for transgression (ta'addi) in giving it away, and the heirs are liable for wrongfully taking it.
This is a benefit of the invalid division: the legatee has multiple avenues for recovery.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قسم الوصيان التركة بين الورثة وأخذ كل واحد منهما نصيب بعضهم فالقسمة فاسدة لأن القسمة لا تكون إلا بين اثنين وكلاهما كشخص واحد لا يملك أحدهما التفرد بالقسمة عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف وإن كان ينفرد أحدهما بالقسمة إلا أن كل واحد وكل صاحبه في القسمة فتصير قسمته مع كقسمته قال مع صاحبه رحمه الله : (فلو قاسم الورثة وأخذ نصيب الموصى له فضاع رجع بثلث ما بقي) أي لو قاسم الوصي الورثة وأخذ نصيب الموصى له فضاع ذلك في يده رجع الموصى له بثلث ما بقي لما بينا أن الموصي له شريك الورثة فيرجع الموصى له على ما في يد الورثة إن كان باقياً فيأخذ بثلثه لعدم صحة القسمة في حقه، وإذا هلك في أيديهم فله أن يضمنهم قدر الثلث ما قبضوا، وإن شاء ضمن الوصي ذلك القدر لأنه متعدٍ فيه بالدفع إليهم والورثة بالقبض فيضمن أيهما شاء
And if two executors divided the estate among the heirs, and each of them took the share of some, the division is invalid because division only occurs between two parties, and both executors are like one person; neither can alone perform the division according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Yusuf, even if one of them can act alone, each is a partner of the other in division, so his division becomes like his division with his partner. He (author of Kanz) said, may Allah have mercy on him: If he divided with the heirs and took the legatee's share, and it perished, he returns with one-third of what remains. That is, if the executor divided with the heirs and took the legatee's share, and it perished in his hand, the legatee returns with one-third of what remains because we have stated that the legatee is a partner of the heirs, so the legatee has recourse to what is in the hands of the heirs if it remains, and he takes one-third of it due to the invalidity of the division in his right. If it perished in their hands, he can hold them liable for the amount of one-third that they took, and if he wishes, he can hold the executor liable for that amount because the executor transgressed by giving it to them, and the heirs by taking it; thus he can hold liable whichever he wishes.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage contains two related rulings. First, regarding division by two executors (wasiyan): they cannot validly divide the estate among the heirs by each taking a portion for themselves, because division requires two distinct parties, and both executors are considered as one person representing the estate. They lack the authority to act on both sides of the division. According to Abu Yusuf, however, one executor may act alone, but if both act together, each is a partner of the other, so the division becomes effectively a division with his partner, which is invalid. Second, the matn from Kanz: if an executor divides the estate with the heirs and takes the legatee's share, and that share perishes in the executor's hand, the legatee has the right to take one-third of what remains of the estate in the hands of the heirs. This is because the legatee is a partner with the heirs (as the bequest is limited to one-third), and the division was invalid with respect to his share. If the property perished in the hands of the heirs, the legatee can hold either the heirs or the executor liable for the value of one-third of what they took. The executor is liable because he transgressed by delivering the property to the heirs; the heirs are liable for taking it. Thus, the legatee has a choice of whom to sue. This ruling underscores the principle that an executor cannot validly distribute the legatee's share without proper authorization, and if loss occurs, the legatee's rights are protected.

Key Terms
وصيان (wasiyan): Two executors appointed by the testator; they are considered as one person regarding the estate's representation.
متعد (muta'addi): Transgressor; one who acts beyond his authority or wrongfully causes loss; executor is muta'addi by improperly distributing property.
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensation; in this context, the legatee can claim compensation from either executor or heirs who wrongfully took the share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two executors divide the estate among themselves, what is the legal status of the division?
A) Valid because executors have authority to distribute
B) Invalid because both represent the same owner and cannot be two parties in division
C) Valid only if the heirs consent
D) Valid if the executors act separately

Key Takeaway
Division by two executors is invalid because they are a single party; the legatee whose share is wrongfully taken can recover from either the executor or heirs.
