Recommended Pace for Completing the Quran: Forty Days for Reflection
Ruling and wisdom behind completing the Quran every forty days.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended period for a hafiz to complete the Quran and explain the underlying rationale of tadabbur.

Core Idea
Quality over speed: completion in forty days ensures reflection, which is the Quran's true purpose.

This short passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the pace of Quran recitation for those who have memorized it. It emphasizes that the goal is not mere haste but deep understanding and contemplation. The author derives a forty-day minimum for completion, supported by a verse from Surah Muhammad that criticizes those who do not ponder.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being ruled upon? For whom? What is the hukm level?
The act is completing the Quran by a hafiz. The ruling is mustahab (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? What type of dalil?
Quranic verse 47:24, which urges pondering.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse lead to the forty-day recommendation?
The verse condemns lack of tadabbur; thus recitation must allow time for reflection, hence a slower pace.
4
Determine the practical quantity
What daily amount is recommended?
One and a half hizbs per day, roughly two-thirds of a juz.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ولحافظ القرآن أن يختم في كل أربعين يوما) لأن المقصود من قراءة القرآن فهم معانيه والاعتبار بما فيه لا مجرد التلاوة قال الله تعالى : أفلا يتدبرون القرآن أم على قلوب إقفالها ﴾ [محمد : ٢٤] وذلك يحصل بالتأني لا بالتواني في المعاني فقدر الختم أقله أربعون يوماً كل يوم حزب ونصف أو ثلثا حزب أو أقل والله تعالى أعلم بالصواب.
He said, may Allah have mercy on him: (For a memorizer of the Quran to complete (recitation) every forty days) because the purpose of reading the Quran is understanding its meanings and taking heed from what is in it, not mere recitation. Allah the Exalted said: 'Do they not ponder over the Quran, or are there locks upon their hearts?' [Muhammad:24]. And that is achieved by deliberateness, not by hastiness in meanings. So the minimum of completion is set at forty days, every day a hizb and a half, or two-thirds of a hizb, or less. And Allah Almighty knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended pace for completing the Quran, particularly for one who has memorized it. The author states that the goal is tadabbur (reflection), not hasty recitation. He supports this with the Quranic verse from Surah Muhammad that criticizes those who do not ponder. Therefore, the minimum period to complete the Quran is forty days, reciting about one and a half hizb daily (or less). This ensures that the recitation is done with contemplation. The ruling is that it is mustahab to take one's time and not rush.

Key Terms
حافظ القرآن (hāfiẓ al-qur'ān): One who has memorized the entire Quran.
ختم (khatm): Completion of recitation of the entire Quran.
حزب (ḥizb): A portion of the Quran; the Quran is divided into 60 hizbs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of days recommended for a hafiz to complete the Quran?
A) Seven days
B) Thirty days
C) Forty days
D) One year

Key Takeaway
A hafiz should aim to complete the Quran every forty days with reflection, as it fulfills the Quranic command to ponder.

Correcting Inheritance Shares When Spouses Are Not Entitled to Return
Procedural ruling on correction with non-radd heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the corrected estate denominator (asl al-mas'alah) when a spouse (non-radd heir) is present with multiple radd-eligible heirs, applying the method of multiplying the spouse's share denominator by the number of radd heirs after reducing for congruence.

Core Idea
When a spouse is present, the return (radd) is only for other heirs; rescale the estate using the spouse’s share denominator and the number of radd heirs.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the procedure for dividing inheritance when some heirs are not entitled to return (radd). Typically, when there is a surplus after Quranic shares, it is returned to the heirs proportionally, but a spouse never receives radd. The author demonstrates how to adjust the estate base (asl al-mas'alah) to ensure the correct distribution when both a spouse and other radd-eligible heirs exist.

Guided Path
1
Identify the non-radd heir and their fixed share
Determine which heir is not entitled to return (spouse). Note the denominator of their share (e.g., 4 for husband, 8 for wife). This denominator becomes the starting point.
The spouse's share is taken from the smallest denominator of their prescribed fraction.
2
List the radd-eligible heirs and count their heads
Identify all heirs eligible for return (e.g., daughters, sisters). Count the total number of such heirs (their 'heads'). This number is used in the multiplication.
If there are multiple types of radd heirs, you may need to combine their shares; here we assume a single type (daughters).
3
Check congruence between the spouse's share remainder and the heir count
After taking the spouse's share, the remainder (in terms of parts from the denominator) and the number of radd heirs may share a common factor. If they do, reduce the heir count by that factor before multiplying.
Congruence (tawafuq) is found when two numbers have a common divisor greater than 1.
4
Multiply to get the corrected estate denominator
Multiply the spouse's share denominator by the (possibly reduced) number of radd heirs. This product is the new asl al-mas'alah that avoids fractions.
If no congruence, multiply by the full count.
5
Distribute the shares
From the corrected estate, give the spouse their fixed share (e.g., 1/4 of the new denominator). The remainder is divided equally among the radd heirs.
Ensure the total distributed equals the corrected estate denominator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عليه اعط فرضه من أقل مخارجه ثم اقسم الباقي على من يرد عليه كزوج وثلاث بنات وإن لم يستقم فإن وافق رؤوسهم في مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه وإلا فاضرب كل عدد رؤوسهم في مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه كزوج وخمس بنات فاضرب وفق بين الباقي من فرض من لا يرد عليه وبين رؤوسهم موافقة فاضرب وفق روؤسهم في مخرج فرض من لا يرد عليه كزوج وست بنات فإن بينهما موافقة في الثلث فرد رؤوسهم إلى اثنين، ثم اضرب به في أربعة وإن لم يوافق الباقي رؤوسهم كزوج وخمس بنات فإنه لا موافقة الخمسة والثلاثة فاضرب جميع رؤوسهن وهو الخمسة في أربعة فالمبلغ في الوجهين المسألة تصحيح فتصح في الأول من ثمانية وفي الوجه الثاني من عشرين لأنك في الأول ضربت اثنين في أربعة وفي الثاني خمسة في أربعة فيأخذ الزوج في الأول سهمين يبقى ستة فكل واحدة من البنات سهم ويأخذ في الثمانية خمسة فيقسم الباقي على خمسة يصيب كل واحدة منهن ثلاثة أسهم.
Upon him (the executor) give his prescribed share from its smallest denominator, then divide the remainder among those entitled to return. For example, a husband and three daughters. If the remainder does not divide evenly, then if it is congruent with the heads (number of heirs) in the denominator of the share of the one not entitled to return, otherwise multiply each number of their heads by the denominator of the share of the one not entitled to return. For example, a husband and five daughters: multiply the congruence between the remainder from the share of the one not entitled to return and their heads, then multiply the congruent part of their heads by the denominator of the share of the one not entitled to return. For example, a husband and six daughters: there is a congruence in one-third, so reduce their heads to two, then multiply it by four. If the remainder does not match their heads, like a husband and five daughters: there is no congruence between five and three, so multiply all their heads, which is five, by four. The total in both cases is the corrected estate. It becomes correct in the first from eight, and in the second from twenty, because in the first you multiplied two by four, and in the second five by four. The husband takes in the first two shares, leaving six, so each daughter gets one share. In the second (five daughters), the husband takes... (text incomplete) actually from eight (the estate of 8), husband takes two shares, leaving six; then from the second (estate of 20), husband takes five (instead of two? wait: the text says: وفي الثاني خمسة في أربعة فيأخذ الزوج في الأول سهمين يبقى ستة فكل واحدة من البنات سهم ويأخذ في الثمانية خمسة فيقسم الباقي على خمسة يصيب كل واحدة منهن ثلاثة أسهم.) Actually, the text is a bit garbled. The intended meaning: In the first case (husband and 3 daughters), the estate is 8, husband gets 2, daughters get 6 (2 each). In the second case (husband and 5 daughters), the estate is 20, husband gets 5 (since his share is 1/4 of 20 = 5), remaining 15 divided among 5 daughters = 3 each.
Source pages p. 414

Key Terms
رَدّ (radd): Return of surplus inheritance to the Quranic sharers proportionally, excluding the spouse.
تصحيح المسألة (tashih al-mas'alah): Adjusting the base denominator of the estate to avoid fractions in shares.
وفق (wafq): Congruence between two numbers having a common divisor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, for a husband and six daughters, what is the corrected estate denominator using the congruence method?
A) 8
B) 24
C) 12
D) 4

Key Takeaway
When a spouse is present, they are excluded from return, so the estate base is adjusted by starting from the spouse's share denominator and multiplying by the number (or reduced number) of radd heirs.
